### v3 cross-doc consistency toggle in bundle-complete (spec-v3 §62) (2026-05-26) — ✅ complete

Closes the last UI affordance of spec-v3 §62 ("A toggle invites the user to run cross-document consistency checks (default on)"). [`src/ui/states.ts`](src/ui/states.ts) bundle-complete template adds a `<label data-role="cross-doc-toggle">` wrapping a checkbox (`[data-role="cross-doc-toggle-input"]`, checked by default). Rendered only when `document_count >= 2`. Flipping the checkbox (a) rewrites the cross-doc summary line in place ("Cross-document consistency disabled." when off; "{N} cross-document finding(s)." / "No cross-document inconsistencies found." when on), (b) invokes the new optional `on_consistency_toggle: (active: boolean) => void` callback on the bundle-complete state. `state.cross_doc_active` (default `true`) seeds the initial UI checkbox state.

Engine side: [`src/ui/pipeline.ts`](src/ui/pipeline.ts) `PipelineOptions` gains `cross_doc_consistency?: boolean`. When set to `false`, `runBundlePipeline` calls `runConsistency` with `rules: []` instead of `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES`, so the consistency pass yields a valid `ConsistencyRun` with empty findings + execution_log and the bundle DOCX/JSON renderer reports "0 cross-document findings".

UI wiring: [`src/ui/main.ts`](src/ui/main.ts) `runBundle` now accepts an `options.cross_doc_consistency` flag, passes it into `runBundlePipeline`, surfaces it on the rendered `bundle-complete` state as `cross_doc_active`, and wires `on_consistency_toggle` to re-run `runBundle(dz, files, { cross_doc_consistency: active })`. The re-run path re-ingests (the bundle pipeline is monolithic today); a future refactor mirroring the single-doc `prepareDocument` / `runReport` split could skip re-ingest the way compliance-frame chip toggles do — flagged in the inline comment.

CSS: [`site/index.html`](site/index.html) gains a `.cross-doc-toggle` rule (min-height 32px for WCAG 2.5.8 target size, 16×16 native checkbox).

Tests: 3 new unit tests in [`src/ui/states.test.ts`](src/ui/states.test.ts) — (1) toggle hidden by default rendering only when `document_count >= 2`, default checked, initial summary reflects findings count; (2) flipping the checkbox rewrites the summary to "Cross-document consistency disabled." and invokes `on_consistency_toggle(false)`, flipping back restores the count and invokes `on_consistency_toggle(true)`; (3) toggle stays hidden when only one document is in the bundle.

`npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green.

### v4 multi-doc offline-verification spec landed (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

[`tests/e2e/v4/no-network.spec.ts`](tests/e2e/v4/no-network.spec.ts) committed. The spec covers LAUNCH row v4-d (spec-v4.md §8 — folder upload / zip / multi-file drop must produce zero cross-origin requests). It mirrors the structure of `tests/e2e/v3/no-network.spec.ts`: load the page, capture all network requests from that point forward, drive the multi-doc drop, wait for a download button, assert valid OOXML zip magic bytes (`PK\x03\x04` + > 1024 bytes), and assert the captured cross-origin request list is empty.

**Forward-compatible probe pattern.** The multi-doc ingest library (`src/ingest/multi.ts`) is production-ready but the live `site/index.html` dropzone (`src/ui/dropzone.ts` `bindDropzone`) still reads only `input.files?.[0]`. The v4 multi-doc DOM affordances — `[data-role="multi-doc-dropzone"]`, `input[type="file"][multiple]` or `input[type="file"][webkitdirectory]` inside `#dropzone`, `[data-role="bundle-download"]` — are not yet wired. The spec probes for any one of these selectors and calls `test.skip` when none are found, matching the pattern in `tests/e2e/v3/a11y-keyboard.spec.ts` for the v3 chip-row probes. The skip is lifted automatically the moment the v4 UI hookup wires `src/ingest/multi.ts` into the live page — no changes to this spec are needed.

**Fixture strategy.** The spec resolves two committed `.docx` fixtures (`tests/fixtures/contracts/mutual-nda.docx` + `tests/fixtures/contracts/bad-nda.docx`). If only one exists, it copies the available fixture to a temp dir under a distinct name so the multi-file input sees two separate logical paths (browsers may deduplicate identical paths in a multi-file `FileList`). If neither fixture exists, the spec skips.

**Gate state.** `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green. `npm run e2e` is not run (Playwright not installed in this env); the spec skips gracefully when the multi-doc UI affordances are absent, so it is safe as a CI gate today and will activate automatically after the UI hookup lands.

### v4 cross-doc bundle expansion + wiring fix (5 → 8) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

**Wiring bug found and fixed.** `tests/golden/v4/bundle.test.ts` was passing `CONSISTENCY_RULES` (V3-only, CC-001 through CC-007) to `runEngineMulti`, meaning no V4 CROSS-* rule had ever fired in the bundle test harness since the bundle test was introduced. The fix: import and use `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES` (the combined `[...V3_CC, ...V4_CROSS]` registry exported from `src/engine/consistency/index.ts`) instead. The V4 rules themselves were correct — the bug was solely in the test wiring.

**Three new bundle fixtures** added under `tests/golden/v4/bundles/`:

- `defined-term-drift/` (msa.txt + dpa.txt) — MSA defines "Customer Data" narrowly (data submitted to the Services); the companion DPA expands it to include personal data, derived analytics, and data generated from end users. Exercises **CROSS-DEFTERM-001** (defined-term semantic drift across documents).
- `missing-companion-dpa/` (msa.txt + sow.txt) — MSA and SOW bundle with no DPA present, even though the MSA explicitly references a Data Processing Agreement as required by applicable law. Exercises **CROSS-MISSING-001** (companion document required but absent from the bundle).
- `precedence-clash/` (msa.txt + sow.txt) — MSA says "this MSA shall control and take precedence over all such documents"; the SOW says "this Statement of Work shall govern and the specific terms herein shall prevail over the general terms of the MSA." Exercises **CROSS-PRECEDENCE-001** (conflicting order-of-precedence clauses across documents).

**Existing five bundles now also surface CROSS findings** (goldens regenerated):

- `cap-mismatch` → `CROSS-AMOUNT-001`, `CROSS-MISSING-001`
- `clean-msa-baa` → `CROSS-MISSING-001`
- `effective-date-paradox` → `CROSS-DATE-001`
- `governing-law-mismatch` → `CC-005`, `CROSS-DATE-001`, `CROSS-JURIS-001`, `CROSS-MISSING-001` (×2)
- `party-name-conflict` → `CROSS-MISSING-001`

Every CROSS rule (all 7: PARTY, JURIS, DEFTERM, DATE, AMOUNT, MISSING, PRECEDENCE) now has at least one dedicated bundle that exercises it end-to-end. The debug scratch test (`tests/debug-cross.test.ts`) is deleted. Full gate green: `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` (2083 passing, 2 skipped).

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (57 → 60) — fourth failure mode (insurance / trust-estate / settlement — every v4 sub-domain now ≥4 fail-fixtures, completing leg 4) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Completes leg 4 of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" upper bound. Adds a fourth failure-mode fixture for the final three v4 sub-domains (insurance, trust-estate, settlement), each exercising a distinct load-bearing rule not covered by any prior fixture. Every v4 sub-domain (B–P) now carries ≥4 end-to-end fail-fixtures. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `insurance-policy-summary-missing-limits-of-liability-fail.txt` — Commercial General Liability Policy Summary with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned coverage-magnitude provision (deliberately avoiding "limits of liability", "limit of liability", "limits of insurance", standalone "limit", "each occurrence", "per claim", and "aggregate"). The Limits-of-Liability section is removed; "per-occurrence deductible" retains a hyphen so the "each occurrence" anchor is not formed. **INS-003** (critical) fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(limits?\s+of\s+(liability|insurance)|limit)/i`, `/(each\s+occurrence|per\s+claim)/i`, and `/(aggregate|general\s+aggregate)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; limits define the insurer's maximum exposure and must appear on the declarations so the insured and contracting parties can verify the coverage stack and total risk-transfer headroom.
- `trust-revocable-living-missing-lifetime-distribution-fail.txt` — Revocable Living Trust with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned provision addressing how the Trustee shall manage trust assets for the Settlor's benefit during the Settlor's life (deliberately avoiding "during settlor's/grantor's lifetime", "while settlor is living", "income", "principal", and "distribut"). The "Distribution Upon Death" section is renamed "Death Disposition" and the operative verb is changed from "distribute" to "pay out". **EST-013** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(during\s+(settlor.?s|grantor.?s)\s+lifetime|while\s+settlor\s+(is\s+)?living)/i` and `/(income|principal|distribut)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; without explicit lifetime-distribution direction, ambiguity about whether the Trustee may distribute principal can defeat estate-planning intent.
- `settlement-mutual-release-missing-scope-of-claims-fail.txt` — Mutual Release with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned scope-of-release clause specifying the breadth of claims discharged (deliberately avoiding "any and all … claims", "each and every … claims", and "known or unknown … claims"). The Release body uses "all claims expressly asserted in the Action" rather than the broad formulation. **SET-002** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(any\s+and\s+all|each\s+and\s+every)\s+claims?/i` and `/(known\s+(or|and)\s+unknown|known\s+or\s+unknown)\s+claims?/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; without explicit scope language a court may construe the release narrowly and leave residual claims alive.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`insurance-policy-summary` / `revocable-living-trust` / `mutual-release`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins sixty fail-fixtures (was fifty-seven); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. Goldens regenerated via `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1`. Full gate green: `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` (2074 passing, 2 skipped). Insurance / trust-estate / settlement now carry four end-to-end fail-fixtures each. Leg 4 complete — every v4 sub-domain now at the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" upper bound.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (54 → 57) — fourth failure mode (ip-licensing / m-and-a / regulatory-prose) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Continues the fourth leg of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" target. Adds a fourth failure-mode fixture for the next three v4 sub-domains (ip-licensing, m-and-a, regulatory-prose), each independent from the prior three and exercising a distinct load-bearing rule not yet covered by any earlier fixture. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `ip-licensing-copyright-missing-section-106-rights-fail.txt` — Author's Rights License Agreement (pinned to `copyright-license` playbook) with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned enumeration of the specific statutory exclusive rights being made available (deliberately avoiding "reproduce/reproduc", "copy", "distribut", "display", "perform", "derivative works", "section 106", and "17 u.s.c. § 106"). "Distributor Inc." is renamed to "Acme Media Holdings Inc." to eliminate the "distribut" substring; the grant clause uses "utilize and exploit commercially" in place of the § 106 enumeration; "Copyright License Agreement" becomes "Author's Rights License Agreement" and all "copyright" occurrences are replaced to eliminate "copy". **IPL-021** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(reproduc|copy|distribut|display|perform|derivative\s+works?)/i` and `/(section\s+106|17\s+u\.?s\.?c\.?\s+§?\s*106)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; 17 U.S.C. § 106 enumerates six exclusive rights and a license that does not enumerate which are granted leaves the scope of permitted use off the four corners.
- `m-and-a-asset-purchase-missing-governing-law-fail.txt` — Asset Purchase Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned choice-of-law and venue-selection provision (deliberately avoiding "governing law", "jurisdiction" near "Delaware"/"Chancery" within 40 chars, and "forum"). The preamble uses "choice-of-law and venue-selection" as a paraphrase so "governing law" never appears; "Delaware corporation" is retained but no "jurisdiction" or "forum" keyword appears within 40 chars of it. **MNA-019** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/governing\s+law/i` and `/(jurisdiction|forum).{0,40}(chancery|delaware)/is` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; Delaware Chancery is the standard forum for private-target M&A and without an explicit governing-law clause the parties face a conflicts-of-laws fight over which state's body of commercial law governs reps, indemnification, and closing mechanics.
- `regulatory-form-d-missing-offering-amount-fail.txt` — Form D Narrative with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned offering-size and investor-floor provision (deliberately avoiding "offering size", "offering amount", "offering aggregate", "minimum investment", "minimum subscription", and any "$NNN" dollar amounts). The Offering Amount section is removed entirely so no dollar amounts appear in the document, and "total capital sought" / "per-investor floor" are used as paraphrases in the preamble. **REG-006** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(offering\s+(size|amount|aggregate))/i`, `/(minimum\s+(investment|subscription))/i`, and `/\$\s*[\d,]+/` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; Form D Items 13–14 require aggregate offering amount and minimum-investment information, and without them the regulator and prospective investors have no four-corners answer to the capital ceiling or buy-in threshold.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`copyright-license` / `asset-purchase-agreement` / `form-d-narrative`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins fifty-seven fail-fixtures (was fifty-four); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. Goldens regenerated via `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1`. Full gate green: `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` (2062 passing, 2 skipped). IP-licensing / m-and-a / regulatory-prose now carry four end-to-end fail-fixtures each.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (51 → 54) — fourth failure mode (compliance / construction / healthcare) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Continues the fourth leg of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" target. Adds a fourth failure-mode fixture for the next three v4 sub-domains (compliance-policy, construction, healthcare), each independent from the prior three and exercising a distinct load-bearing rule not yet covered by any earlier fixture. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `compliance-anti-bribery-missing-gifts-hospitality-fail.txt` — Anti-Bribery Policy with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned things-of-value provision (deliberately avoiding "gifts", "gift", "hospitality", "entertainment", "meals", "charitable", "political contribution", "threshold", "pre-approval", and "recordkeeping" — using paraphrases "courtesy items", "social-function invitations", "philanthropic and electoral-giving contributions", "per-occasion dollar caps", "advance-authorization workflows", and "logging obligations" instead). **POL-011** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(gifts?|hospitality|entertainment|meals)/i`, `/(charitable|political\s+contribution)/i`, and `/(threshold|pre.?approval|recordkeeping)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; gifts and hospitality to foreign officials are the most common FCPA risk area (DOJ-SEC FCPA Resource Guide ch. 2) and without a policy setting monetary thresholds, a pre-approval workflow, and recordkeeping requirements, the compliance program has no operational control over the highest-frequency corruption vector.
- `construction-contract-missing-scope-of-work-fail.txt` — Construction Contract with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned work-description and document-hierarchy provision (deliberately avoiding "scope of the work", "scope of work", "work to be performed", "contract documents", "drawings and specifications", and "specifications"). **CON-002** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(scope\s+of\s+(the\s+)?work|work\s+to\s+be\s+performed)/i` and `/(contract\s+documents|drawings\s+and\s+specifications|specifications)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; AIA A201 § 1.1.1 defines the Contract Documents (Agreement + Conditions + Drawings + Specifications + addenda + Modifications) and without an enumerated scope and document hierarchy neither party has a four-corners answer to what the contractor is obligated to build or which drawings and specs govern change-order disputes.
- `healthcare-phi-authorization-missing-conditioning-statement-fail.txt` — PHI Authorization with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned conditioning-prohibition provision (deliberately avoiding "treatment", "payment", "enrollment", "eligibility", "benefits", "not conditioned", "cannot refuse", and "cannot condition"). The Patient Rights section is rewritten to remove "treatment" and "conditioned"; the Description section replaces "treatment notes" with "clinical notes". **HC-016** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(treatment|payment|enrollment|eligibility|benefits)/i` and `/(not\s+conditioned|cannot\s+(refuse|condition)|will\s+not\s+(affect|condition))/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; 45 C.F.R. § 164.508(c)(2)(ii) requires a statement that treatment, payment, enrollment, or eligibility for benefits is not conditioned on the authorization — without one the patient cannot verify that refusing to sign carries no care-denial consequence.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`anti-bribery-policy` / `construction-contract` / `phi-authorization`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins fifty-four fail-fixtures (was fifty-one); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. - `equity-safe-missing-liquidity-event-fail.txt` — SAFE with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned exit-event treatment provision (deliberately avoiding "liquidity event", "change of control", and "acquisition"). - `real-estate-net-lease-missing-maintenance-repair-fail.txt` — Triple Net Lease with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned upkeep-and-remediation provision (deliberately avoiding "maintenance and repair", "roof", "structural integrity", and "structural repair"). The preamble is extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned governance-body composition and election article, relying instead on the residual authority supplied by DGCL § 141 and the certificate of incorporation. **GOV-006** (critical) fires because its two `present_patterns` `/board\s+of\s+directors/i` and `/(elect|appoint).{0,30}directors?/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; DGCL § 141(b) and MBCA § 8.03 require the bylaws (or charter) to fix the number of directors and the manner of election — without a board-composition clause the proxy materials and internal records have no four-corners anchor for board size or election procedure.

- `privacy-cookie-notice-missing-consent-mechanism-fail.txt` — Cookie Notice with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned opt-in mechanism section, relying instead on users' browser settings and supervisory-authority guidance. The Consent and Withdrawal sections are removed; "cookie management tool" is absent. No "consent", "banner", "preference center", "cookie preference", "accept", "reject", or "manage" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **PRV-002** (critical) fires because its three `present_patterns` `/consent/i`, `/(banner|preference\s+center|cookie\s+preference)/i`, and `/(accept|reject|manage)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; ePrivacy Art. 5(3) + GDPR Art. 7 require freely given, specific, informed, and unambiguous affirmative-action consent (CJEU *Planet49*) — routing users to generic browser controls satisfies neither the granular opt-in requirement nor the equal-prominence withdraw standard EDPB Guidelines 5/2020 contemplate.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (42 → 45) — third failure mode (ip-licensing / m-and-a / insurance, via new sub-playbooks) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Completes the third leg of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" target across **every** v4 sub-domain. The remaining three sub-domains (ip-licensing, m-and-a, insurance) each had only one silent presence-rule slot left on their existing playbook (copyright-license / asset-purchase-agreement / insurance-policy-summary) and that slot was either unfireable (IPL-021's `/copy/` matches "copyright") or covered. This batch therefore widens each sub-domain to a **second playbook** within the same family, yielding the third fixture per sub-domain. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `ip-licensing-patent-missing-licensed-patents-fail.txt` — Patent License Agreement (pinned to the `patent-license` playbook, a different IPL sub-domain playbook from the copyright-license series). The Exhibit reference uses "Exhibit A" rather than "Schedule A" to avoid the rule's `/schedule\s+a/i` anchor, and the preamble uses the paraphrase "industrial-monopoly grants" so the literal anchor "licensed patents" does not appear anywhere in the document. **IPL-007** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(licensed\s+patents?|schedule\s+a)/i` and `/(patent\s+no|u\.?s\.?\s+pat|application\s+no)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; patent licenses must identify the licensed claims with sufficient specificity for both enforcement and royalty accounting.
- `m-and-a-loi-missing-binding-demarcation-fail.txt` — Letter of Intent (pinned to the `loi-term-sheet` playbook). The doc affirmatively states it "is binding upon the parties" and includes a Confidentiality section — pattern 2 and pattern 3 of MNA-001 match, but pattern 1 (`/(non.?binding|not\s+binding|except\s+(as|for))/i`) does not, so the compound rule's `min_match=3` threshold is missed (2/3) and **MNA-001** fires. The *SIGA / Pennzoil* line shows that LOIs can be enforced as binding contracts if the parties do not clearly disclaim intent to be bound on commercial terms — a doc that says only "is binding upon the parties" without demarcating the non-binding commercial provisions invites unintended enforcement.
- `insurance-endorsement-coverage-restricting-fail.txt` — Endorsement (pinned to the `insurance-endorsement` playbook) styled as a Commercial General Liability Endorsement — Absolute Pollution Exclusion. The body affirmatively states "This endorsement is an absolute exclusion of pollution and applies in addition to all other terms of the Policy" — the language-rule's first bad pattern `/(absolute\s+exclusion|total\s+exclusion).{0,80}(pollution|cyber|communicable\s+disease|silica|asbestos|abuse|molest)/is` matches and **INS-010** fires. Coverage-restricting endorsements (absolute pollution / cyber / communicable-disease exclusions, $25K sublimits) materially shrink coverage and should be flagged to underwriters and the broker.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`patent-license` / `loi-term-sheet` / `insurance-endorsement`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins forty-five fail-fixtures (was forty-two); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. Goldens regenerated via `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1`. The Release body uses bare "Plaintiff / Defendant" language without any extended-identification recitations. **SET-001** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/releas(or|ee|ing\s+part(y|ies)|ed\s+part(y|ies))/i` and `/(affiliates?|subsidiaries|officers|directors|agents)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; an effective release must bind every entity intended to benefit — failure to enumerate affiliates, officers, directors, agents, and assigns leaves residual claims against unnamed parties.

The Books-and-Records section is removed entirely. **POL-008** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(books\s+and\s+records|accounting\s+(records|controls))/i`, `/(internal\s+(accounting\s+)?controls?|78m)/i`, and `/(accurate|accuracy)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; 15 U.S.C. § 78m(b)(2) requires issuers to maintain accurate books and records and adequate internal accounting controls — violations can be charged without underlying bribery, so the policy must affirmatively address the accounting-provisions half of FCPA enforcement.
- `construction-contract-missing-indemnification-insurance-fail.txt` — Construction Contract with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned risk-allocation provision (deliberately avoiding "indemnify", "indemnification", "insurance", "CGL", "workers compensation", and "waiver of subrogation"). Oblig. § 5-322.1, TX Ins. § 151) void indemnity for owner's own / sole negligence — the carve-outs must be in the contract, a separate Owner-Controlled Risk Management Program is not a substitute.
- `healthcare-phi-authorization-missing-purpose-fail.txt` — PHI Authorization with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned reason-for-disclosure provision (deliberately avoiding "purpose", "at the request of", and "for litigation / life insurance / treatment / payment / research / marketing"). The Purpose section is removed, "treatment notes" in the Description is changed to "clinical notes" so `for treatment` cannot match, and the Recipient is renamed from "Insurance Underwriter Inc." to "Acme Underwriting Inc." so "for life insurance" never appears. **HC-013** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/purpose/i` and `/(at\s+the\s+request\s+of|for\s+(litigation|life\s+insurance|treatment|payment|research|marketing))/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; 45 C.F.R. § 164.508(c)(1)(iv) requires a description of each purpose, and an authorization without one fails the meaningful-and-specific standard and is unenforceable on its face.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (30 → 33) — third failure mode (governance / employment / privacy) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Begins the third leg of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" target. - `governance-bylaws-overbroad-exclusive-forum-fail.txt` — Bylaws with the preamble narrating a comprehensive exclusive-forum election and a new Exclusive Forum section designating the Court of Chancery of the State of Delaware as the exclusive forum for any claim asserted against the corporation, including without limitation any claim arising under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 or any other federal securities laws. **GOV-011** fires because its bad-language pattern `/exclusive\s+forum.{0,120}(state\s+of\s+delaware|chancery).{0,200}(exchange\s+act|1934\s+act|federal\s+securities)/is` matches; *Salzberg v. Sciabacucchi* (Del. 2020) upheld Delaware-forum bylaws for Securities Act of 1933 claims but expressly declined to extend that holding to Exchange Act claims (which carry exclusive federal-court jurisdiction under § 27) — an exclusive-forum bylaw that purports to capture Exchange Act claims is at risk of being struck on petition. This is the second **language-quality** (bad-pattern present) row-b fail; every prior governance/employment/privacy entry was a presence-rule (clause missing) fail.
- `employment-executive-missing-restrictive-covenants-fail.txt` — Executive Employment Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned post-employment-behavior provision (avoiding the rule's anchor phrases by paraphrase: "constraining the Executive's ability to compete", "communicate confidential information", "recruit Employer personnel after termination"). The Restrictive Covenants section is removed entirely. **EMP-008** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/restrictive\s+covenant/i` and `/(non.?disclosure|non.?solicit)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; executives need NDA + non-solicit (and non-compete only where enforceable) coverage, and without an in-document restrictive-covenants clause or reference the Employer's post-termination protections rest entirely off the four corners.
- `privacy-cookie-notice-missing-third-party-recipients-fail.txt` — Cookie Notice with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned downstream-disclosure provision (deliberately avoiding "third-party", "recipients", "international transfers", "outside the EU/EEA/UK", "SCC", "DPF", and "Data Privacy Framework" — the preamble uses "downstream-counterparty identification" so neither "recipients" nor "third-party" appears anywhere in the document). The Third-Party Cookies section is removed. **PRV-006** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(third.?party|recipients?)/i`, `/(international\s+transfers?|outside\s+the\s+(eu|eea|uk))/i`, and `/(scc|dpf|data\s+privacy\s+framework)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; GDPR Art. 13(1)(e)–(f) requires disclosure of recipients and international-transfer mechanisms, and cookie data routinely flows to third-party analytics / ad-tech in the US and elsewhere.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (27 → 30) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v4-b coverage from twenty-seven end-to-end fail-fixtures to thirty by adding a second failure-mode fixture for the final three v4 sub-domains (insurance, trust-estate, settlement). With this batch every v4 sub-domain (B–P) now carries at least two end-to-end fail-fixtures, completing the second leg of the spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" target across the full v4 family. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `insurance-policy-summary-missing-named-insured-fail.txt` — Commercial General Liability Policy Summary derived from the existing premium-deductible fail-fixture by renaming the "Named Insured" line to "Insured Party" and the "Producer" line to "Insurance Intermediary" (with the broker entity renamed to "Insurance Wholesale Services LLC" so neither "broker" nor "agent" appears anywhere in the document). The preamble narrates the affirmative election not to include a party-and-intermediary identification provision. **INS-001** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/named\s+insured/i` and `/(producer|broker|agent)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; coverage rights run to the Named Insured under state insurance codes, and without a clearly labelled "Named Insured" and a stated producer / broker the declarations are off the four corners.
- `trust-revocable-living-missing-death-distribution-fail.txt` — Revocable Living Trust with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned post-passing apportionment provision (deliberately avoiding "upon settlor's death", "after death", "beneficiar", and "distribute"). The Distribution-Upon-Death section is removed entirely so neither "distribute" nor "beneficiary" appears anywhere in the document. **EST-014** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(upon\s+(settlor.?s|grantor.?s)\s+death|after\s+death)/i` and `/(beneficiar|distribute)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; the post-death disposition is the trust's principal estate-planning function, and without named beneficiaries and stated shares the trust corpus is at risk of intestate disposition through the pour-over will rather than the planned distribution.
- `settlement-confidential-overbroad-future-claims-fail.txt` — Confidential Settlement Agreement and Mutual Release (pinned to the `mutual-release` playbook since SET-005 applies only to that playbook id) with the preamble extended by a sentence affirmatively electing to extend the release beyond the conduct underlying the Action to bind the releasing party with respect to prospective claims of any kind whatsoever, and the Mutual Release section amplified with "any future claims that may arise hereafter against the other party, including any prospective claims of any kind whatsoever". This is the first **language-quality** (bad-pattern present) v4 row-b fail-fixture — every prior entry has been a presence-rule (clause missing) fail. **SET-005** fires because its two bad-language patterns `/releases?.{0,80}(future|hereafter\s+arising|may\s+arise).{0,80}claims?/is` and `/(future|prospective)\s+claims?.{0,80}(of\s+any\s+kind|whatsoever)/is` both match; California Civ. Code § 1668 voids contracts that exempt a party from responsibility for their own fraud, willful injury, or violation of law, and many jurisdictions are skeptical of releases of unaccrued claims — a release that purports to cover post-execution conduct is at risk of being limited or voided.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`insurance-policy-summary` / `revocable-living-trust` / `mutual-release`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins thirty fail-fixtures (was twenty-seven); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. Goldens regenerated via `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1`. Full gate green: `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` (test count captured in commit message). **Milestone:** every v4 sub-domain (B–P) now carries at least two end-to-end fail-fixtures, completing the second leg of spec §16 "2–4 fixtures per family" across the full v4 family.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (24 → 27) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v4-b coverage from twenty-four end-to-end fail-fixtures to twenty-seven by adding a second failure-mode fixture for the next three v4 sub-domains (ip-licensing, m-and-a, regulatory-prose), each deriving from the corresponding minimal-pass fixture by extending the preamble with a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a second load-bearing clause and dropping every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `ip-licensing-copyright-missing-term-territory-media-fail.txt` — Copyright License Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned enumeration of the geographic-and-durational scope of the license. The Term-and-Termination section is renamed "Duration and Discontinuance" and the Licensee is renamed from "Acme Media Inc." to "Acme Studios Inc." so the substring `media` does not appear anywhere in the document. **IPL-022** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(term|territor)/i`, `/(media|channels?|format)/i`, and `/(now\s+known|hereafter\s+developed)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; term + territory + media define the boundary of the license — open-ended grants in unfamiliar media invite *Bourne v. Walt Disney*-style disputes when new exploitation surfaces emerge, and an in-document scope must control over a separately negotiated rate card. (IPL-021 was the original target but its `/copy/i` sub-pattern matches the substring "copy" anywhere in the document — including the word "copyright" — so it can never fire on a copyright license; this is a known limitation of the rule's regex and is recorded here for future tightening.)
- `m-and-a-asset-purchase-missing-assumed-liabilities-fail.txt` — Asset Purchase Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned schedule enumerating the specific liability categories that Buyer is contractually undertaking at the Closing, relying instead on Schedule 2.4 and Schedule 2.5 to list the closed sets without using the term "Assumed Liabilities". The Assumed-Liabilities body becomes a "Retained Obligations" section so no "assumed liabilities" anchor remains. **MNA-022** fires because its `present_pattern` `/assumed\s+liabilities/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document; the structural advantage of an APA is that Buyer assumes only specifically-identified liabilities, and without an Assumed Liabilities clause the implicit carve-in fails and Buyer faces ambiguity about which Seller obligations transfer at Closing.
- `regulatory-form-d-missing-bad-actor-fail.txt` — Form D Narrative with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned screening-and-disclosure provision addressing Rule 506(d) bad-actor disqualification, relying instead on the Issuer's separately executed officer-and-director questionnaires and outside-counsel sign-off. The Bad-Actor Disqualification section is removed. **REG-005** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(bad.actor|rule\s+506\(d\)|disqualif)/i` and `/(covered\s+persons?|disqualifying\s+events?)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; Rule 506(d) disqualifies covered persons (directors, officers, 20%+ owners) with disqualifying events from relying on Rule 506, and an issuer that omits the screening recital cannot show it performed the reasonable-care diligence the rule contemplates.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`copyright-license` / `asset-purchase-agreement` / `form-d-narrative`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins twenty-seven fail-fixtures (was twenty-four); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. ### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (21 → 24) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v4-b coverage from twenty-one end-to-end fail-fixtures to twenty-four by adding a second failure-mode fixture for the next three v4 sub-domains (compliance-policy, construction, healthcare), each deriving from the corresponding minimal-pass fixture by extending the preamble with a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a second load-bearing clause and dropping every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. - `compliance-anti-bribery-missing-ukba-cross-border-fail.txt` — Anti-Bribery Policy with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned non-US-statute applicability provision, relying instead on the Compliance Officer's quarterly memorandum and the Company's separately published Global Code of Conduct. The Compliance-with-Law section drops the UKBA reference. **POL-010** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(uk\s+bribery\s+act|ukba|bribery\s+act\s+2010)/i` and `/(failure\s+to\s+prevent|cross.border|adequate\s+procedures)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; UKBA is broader than FCPA (commercial bribery + corporate "failure to prevent" offense + no facilitating-payments exception + broad jurisdictional reach), and the SFO has used the corporate-offense theory in active enforcement since 2017.
- `construction-contract-missing-time-of-completion-fail.txt` — Construction Contract with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned schedule-and-delay-remedy provision, relying instead on the Project Manager's published schedule of values and the separately executed Master Schedule. The Schedule section is removed and the Payment section's retainage anchor reads "until Final Acceptance" instead of "until Substantial Completion". **CON-004** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(substantial\s+completion|final\s+completion|completion\s+date)/i` and `/(liquidated\s+damages|delay\s+damages|no\s+damages\s+for\s+delay)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; AIA A101 § 3 requires commencement, substantial-completion, and final-completion dates — schedule slip is the single largest source of construction disputes and without those anchors owner-suffered delay damages have no contractually defined trigger.
- `healthcare-phi-authorization-missing-right-to-revoke-fail.txt` — PHI Authorization with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned cancellation-mechanic provision, relying instead on the Covered Entity's published Notice of Privacy Practices and the Privacy Officer's standard intake procedures. The Expiration section drops the revocation sentence; the Patient Rights section replaces "except as permitted by" with "subject to the limits set forth in" to avoid the "except" anchor. **HC-015** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/(revoke|revoking|revocation)/i`, `/(in\s+writing|written\s+notice)/i`, and `/(except|reliance)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; 45 C.F.R. § 164.508(c)(2)(i) requires a statement of the right to revoke in writing and the exceptions — without one, the patient has no four-corners hook to withdraw consent and the covered entity has no instruction for when reliance-based disclosures may still proceed.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning the v4 playbook (`anti-bribery-policy` / `construction-contract` / `phi-authorization`). - `employment-executive-missing-base-salary-fail.txt` — Executive Employment Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned cash-compensation schedule, relying instead on a separately executed compensation letter and the Employer's standard payroll practices. **EMP-002** fires because its three `present_patterns` `/base\s+salary/i`, `/annual\s+(bonus|incentive)/i`, and `/target\s+bonus/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; Reg S-K Item 402 requires disclosure of compensation arrangements for named executive officers, and without a stated base salary and bonus structure the central economic terms of the engagement are off the four corners.
- `privacy-cookie-notice-missing-withdraw-consent-fail.txt` — Cookie Notice with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned consent-withdrawal section, relying instead on the user's ability to clear stored cookies through browser controls and lodge a supervisory-authority complaint. **PRV-004** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(withdraw|change|update|revoke).{0,40}consent/i` and `/(cookie\s+(preferences?|settings)|preference\s+center)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; GDPR Art. 7(3) requires that withdrawing consent be as easy as giving it, and routing the user to generic browser controls fails the equal-prominence standard EDPB Guidelines 5/2020 contemplate.

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (12 → 15) (2026-05-22) — ✅ complete

- `insurance-policy-summary-missing-premium-deductible-fail.txt` — Commercial General Liability Policy Summary with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned economic-terms provision (deliberately avoiding "premium", "deductible", "self-insured retention", and "SIR"). **INS-004 (critical)** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/premium/i` and `/(deductible|self.?insured\s+retention|sir)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; without a stated premium and the insured's retained-risk threshold, the parties cannot verify the consideration paid or the attachment point at which the insurer's payment obligation begins.
- `regulatory-form-d-missing-exemption-fail.txt` — Form D Narrative with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned safe-harbor-identification provision (deliberately avoiding "Rule 504 / 506 / 506(b) / 506(c)" and "exempt / exemption"). **REG-002** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/(rule\s+50[46]|rule\s+506\(b\)|rule\s+506\(c\))/i` and `/(exempt|exemption)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; Form D Item 6 requires identification of the exemption claimed, and the difference between 506(b) (no general solicitation, reasonable belief) and 506(c) (general solicitation permitted, verified accredited status) is the central regulatory question for a Reg D offering.
- `trust-revocable-living-missing-spendthrift-fail.txt` — Revocable Living Trust with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned third-party-claim-protection provision (deliberately avoiding "spendthrift", "creditor", "involuntary transfer", and "attachment"). **EST-016** fires because its two `present_patterns` `/spendthrift/i` and `/(creditor|involuntary\s+transfer|attachment)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document; UTC § 502 enforces spendthrift provisions restraining both voluntary and involuntary transfers of beneficial interests, and without one a beneficiary's judgment creditors can reach the beneficial interest and defeat the trust's estate-planning purpose.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar forcing the v4 playbook (so the auto-detector cannot route to `generic-fallback`). Vaulytica's own pipeline code is its own ~115 KB chunk. With the year-long immutable cache from Step 14, a bump to one dep only invalidates that chunk for returning users. ### STRUCT-013 placeholder rule + 81-rule registry (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added **STRUCT-013 — Unfilled template placeholders (critical, structural)** to push `bad-nda.docx` detection to **4/5** intentional violations. Regex coverage: `[insert …]`, `[Title-Case Name]`, `[TBD]` / `[REDACTED]` / `[PLACEHOLDER]` / `[PENDING]` / `[TBA]` / `[FILL IN]` / `[TODO]`, `{{mustache}}`, `<<angle>>`, `XXX`-runs of 3+ uppercase X, underscore-line placeholders of 10+ chars. Doesn't fire on `[1]` or `[a]` footnotes. Wired into `LAUNCH_RULES` (now **81 rules**), the 80→81 count assertion in `all-rules.test.ts` updated, 9 dedicated rule tests added, `fixture-sanity.test.ts` updated, goldens regenerated.

### Subresource Integrity (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Closed the SRI hardening item from `docs/threat-model.md`. New `subresourceIntegrity` Vite plugin runs after `deployAssets` and rewrites every same-origin `<script src=…>` and `<link rel="modulepreload|preload|stylesheet" href=…>` in `dist/index.html` to carry an `integrity="sha384-…"` + `crossorigin="anonymous"` pair derived from the on-disk asset bytes. If the served bytes don't hash to the declared value, the browser refuses to execute the bundle. `tests/integration/sri.test.ts` runs `npm run build` end-to-end and verifies (1) the integrity attribute is present, (2) the hash matches `sha384(disk)` byte-for-byte, (3) no malformed integrity attrs, (4) the main asset is non-trivial in size. `threat-model.md` updated: "Vaulytica-tampered builds" section now says SRI hardens the entry; "Verification procedure" gains step 6 (view source on the live site, recompute locally to compare).

### FIN-001/002 skip-lift on NDA playbooks (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Both rules have narrow pattern matchers that only fire on monetary content actually appearing in the document, so the original "skip on NDAs to avoid false positives" was over-cautious. `mutual-nda.json` and `unilateral-nda.json` no longer skip FIN-001 or FIN-002; FIN-003 through FIN-008 (fees, payment terms, late fees, etc.) remain skipped because they legitimately don't apply. **`bad-nda.docx` intentional-violation detection: 4/5 → 5/5** (full coverage; the previously-unaddressed word/numeral mismatch `fifty thousand dollars ($75,000)` now fires under FIN-001). Sanity guard updated; goldens regenerated.

### Rule catalog expansion to 83 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added two new rules:
- **DARK-005 — Class-action waiver (critical, dark-patterns)**: catches `waives class action`, `gives up collective action`, `no class action`, `on an individual basis only`. Cites the FTC deception statement; relevant since Concepcion (2011) + Epic Systems (2018). 6 dedicated tests.
- **STRUCT-014 — Inconsistent defined-term casing (info, structural)**: when `"Confidential Information"` is defined but `confidential information` (lowercase) appears elsewhere, flags the slip. Skips single-word defined terms and sentence-start lowercase. 5 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **83 rules**; all count assertions in `all-rules.test.ts` bumped (81→83 + describe header). Goldens regenerated.

### Rule catalog expansion to 86 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added three more rules:
- **TEMP-011 — Auto-renewal notice window under 30 days (warning, temporal)**: parses the number of days from the non-renewal notice clause and fires when < 30. Cites FTC Negative Option Rule (`stat-16-cfr-425`). The example rule from `docs/adding-a-rule.md` is now a real implementation; the doc was updated to point at the shipped code and to use the actual `emit(ctx, rule, …)` helper signature. 5 dedicated tests.
- **RISK-015 — Indemnification without aggregate cap (warning, risk-allocation)**: fires when indemnification language is present and either no cap exists or the cap explicitly carves out indemnification (`limited to twelve months… except for indemnification obligations`). 5 dedicated tests.
- **DARK-006 — Asymmetric pre-suit notice / cure window (warning, dark-patterns)**: detects clauses requiring one party (Customer / Employee / Licensee / Tenant / Contractor / Consumer / User / Buyer) to give pre-suit notice or a cure period, without imposing the same gate on the drafter. Skips bilateral framings like `each party shall…`. 4 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **86 rules**; all count assertions in `all-rules.test.ts` bumped (83→86 + describe header). Goldens regenerated.

### Rule catalog expansion to 89 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added three more rules in under-covered categories (obligations / ip-and-data / choice-and-venue):
- **OBLI-007 — Material Adverse Change clause present (warning, obligations)**: surfaces `material adverse change` / `material adverse effect` / `MAC event` for explicit review. Doesn't fire on bare `material breach`. 5 dedicated tests.
- **IPDATA-007 — Data retention period unspecified (warning, ip-and-data)**: fires when the contract handles data (Customer Data / personal data / PII / DPA / data processing) but no clause specifies retention duration, deletion, return-or-destroy, or purge. Aligns with GDPR Art. 5(1)(e) and CCPA retention-definition expectations. 5 dedicated tests.
- **CHOICE-009 — Governing law differs from venue jurisdiction (info, choice-and-venue)**: surfaces contracts where the choice-of-law jurisdiction is different from the venue / forum jurisdiction. Uses the jurisdictions extractor's normalized `jurisdiction_id` when available; falls back to text comparison. 4 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **89 rules**; all count assertions in `all-rules.test.ts` bumped (86→89 + describe header). Goldens regenerated.

### Rule catalog expansion to 95 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added three more rules in lighter categories:
- **FIN-009 — Late fee above 18%/year (warning, financial)**: parses month/year/day-period rates, normalizes to annual, fires when > 18%. Cites N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-501. 6 dedicated tests.
- **IPDATA-008 — Cross-border data transfer without safeguard (warning, ip-and-data)**: fires when transfer-outside-EEA/EU/UK/US language appears without SCCs / BCRs / adequacy decision / DPF / Article 46 reference. 6 dedicated tests.
- **RISK-016 — Insurance requirement without coverage minimum (warning, risk-allocation)**: fires when `maintain insurance` appears without a `$X per occurrence`, `at least $X`, or `not less than $X` minimum. 6 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **95 rules**; count assertions bumped (92→95 + describe header). Goldens regenerated.

### Rule catalog expansion to 98 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added three more rules covering personnel, dark-patterns, and temporal gaps:
- **PERS-006 — Non-disparagement clause present (warning, personnel)**: surfaces non-disparagement language for review against NLRB *McLaren Macomb* (Feb 2023) and SEC Rule 21F-17. 4 dedicated tests.
- **DARK-007 — Browsewrap / passive-acceptance language (warning, dark-patterns)**: detects passive-consent constructs (`by using the Service`, `continued use constitutes acceptance`, `deemed to have agreed`). Cites *Specht v. Netscape*, *Nguyen v. Barnes & Noble*, *Berkson v. Gogo*. 5 dedicated tests.
- **TEMP-012 — Survival clause silent on sticky obligations (warning, temporal)**: when survival language exists AND confidentiality / IP / indemnity language exists, the rule names every sticky obligation the survival clause failed to enumerate. 5 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **98 rules**; count assertions bumped (95→98 + describe header). Goldens regenerated.

### 🎯 100-rule milestone (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Two final rules to reach the round number:
- **OBLI-008 — Efforts standard undefined (info, obligations)**: surfaces `best efforts` / `commercially reasonable efforts` / `reasonable efforts` / `good faith efforts` / `diligent efforts` when no in-document definition exists. Different efforts-standard phrases carry materially different obligation strengths (*Bloor v. Falstaff*, 2d Cir. 1979). 5 dedicated tests.
- **CHOICE-010 — Asymmetric jury-trial waiver (warning, choice-and-venue)**: fires when a jury-trial waiver binds one named party without binding the drafter. Cites *Leasing Service Corp. v. Crane* (4th Cir. 1986). 5 dedicated tests.

`LAUNCH_RULES` now ships **100 rules** (was 80 at v1.0.0 — +25%); count assertions bumped (98→100 + describe header). Goldens regenerated. **370/370 passing + 2 intentional skips.** All ten rule categories better-covered than launch:

|----------|--------|-----|
| Structural | 12 | 15 |
| Financial | 8 | 9 |
| Temporal | 10 | 12 |
| Obligations | 6 | 8 |
| Risk allocation | 14 | 16 |
| Choice and venue | 8 | 10 |
| Termination | 8 | 9 |
| IP and data | 6 | 8 |
| Personnel | 4 | 6 |
| Dark patterns | 4 | 7 |
| **Total** | **80** | **100** |

### Fixture corpus expanded to 5 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

`tests/fixtures/build-fixtures.ts` now produces a 5th synthetic fixture, **`bad-employment.docx`**, targeting the `employment-at-will-us` playbook (no fixture previously exercised this surface). The fixture carries 7 intentional violations sized to exercise the post-1.0 personnel/dark-pattern rules: California non-compete (PERS-005), non-disparagement without NLRA/SEC carve-outs (PERS-006), asymmetric termination-for-convenience (TERM-009), one-sided jury-trial waiver (CHOICE-010), undefined `best efforts` (OBLI-008), class-action waiver (DARK-005), survival clause silent on confidentiality + IP (TEMP-012). All 7 fire and are locked in by `tests/integration/fixture-sanity.test.ts`. The matched playbook is correctly `employment-at-will-us` (confidence 0.875). Golden + 8 new sanity assertions added.

### Fixture corpus expanded to 7 (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added **`bad-lease.docx`** (lease-commercial-multitenant playbook @ 0.7 confidence) and **`bad-contractor.docx`** (independent-contractor playbook @ 0.8 confidence). bad-lease carries 7 commercial-real-estate-specific violations (Premises placeholder, 10-day non-renewal window, 36%/year late fee, bare insurance clause, uncapped indemnification, asymmetric pre-suit notice, one-sided jury waiver) — all 7 fire. bad-contractor sets up the misclassification dark pattern (fixed hours, company tools, exclusivity) and surfaces the policy concern through 5 rules. Sanity-guard entries added; goldens generated. Pushes the row-(m) corpus from **5 → 7 fixtures**.

### 🎯 Fixture corpus reaches 10 (spec §27 row-(m) target hit) (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Three more synthetic fixtures: **`bad-unilateral-nda.docx`** (unilateral-nda playbook @ 1.0 confidence), **`bad-residential-lease.docx`** (lease-residential-us @ 1.0), **`bad-msa.docx`** (msa-general @ 1.0). All 16 newly-required rules across the three sanity-guard entries fire. **Corpus: 7 → 10 fixtures. Spec §27 row-(m) target reached.** Direct playbook fixture coverage: 8 of 12 launch playbooks (mutual-nda, unilateral-nda, employment-at-will-us, independent-contractor, saas-customer, msa-general, lease-commercial-multitenant, lease-residential-us). LAUNCH.md row (m) flipped from ⚠️ deferred → ✅ pass.

Two adjacent fixes shipped alongside the fixtures:
- **Pipeline body-text bug**: both `src/ui/pipeline.ts` and `tests/integration/_pipeline-helpers.ts` were walking only `sections[0]` for the body text passed to `matchPlaybook`. Caused unilateral NDAs to match mutual-nda (the unilateral-specific phrasing like `the Disclosing Party` lives deeper in the doc). Both helpers now recursively walk every section + child paragraph. `bad-unilateral-nda.docx` now matches `unilateral-nda` at 1.0 confidence instead of mutual-nda at 0.8.
- **FIN-009 regex**: `Late fee: 5% per month` (with colon) slipped through. The `\s+` between the keyword and the rate was tightened to `[:\s]`. Caught by the `bad-residential-lease.docx` sanity guard.

**394/394 passing + 2 intentional skips.**

Together with the existing single-machine determinism triple-guard (`all-rules.test.ts` + `golden-output.test.ts` + `determinism-guard.test.ts`), this gives the cross-machine verification the spec §17 / row (c) is asking for. Row flips to ✅ pass on the first all-green workflow run.

Caught the missing `author` on TechArticle — fixed in `site/index.html` by attributing the article to the Vaulytica organization. The live Google Rich Results probe still has to run against the deployed URL, but the static-shape half is machine-enforced now.

**402/402 passing + 2 intentional skips.**

The formal axe DevTools audit still runs against the deployed page.

20 new tests; both rows now have a static-shape guard that catches regressions in CI before they ship. **422/422 passing + 2 intentional skips.**

### PERS-007 (rule 101) + bad-saas-vendor + bad-consulting (corpus 10 → 12) (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Added **PERS-007 — IC misclassification signals (warning, personnel; 101st rule)**: fires when a worker is labeled `independent contractor` AND ≥2 employee-indicator clauses appear (fixed daily hours, company-supplied equipment, daily reporting, exclusivity, salary-like flat monthly retainer, required on-site presence). Cites IRS 20-factor + DOL economic-realities + CA AB-5 + MA prong-B tests. 6 dedicated tests.

Added **`bad-saas-vendor.docx`** (vendor-side SaaS — aggressive uptime via best efforts, IP indemnity carved out of cap) and **`bad-consulting.docx`** (hybrid IC + advisory with classic misclassification dark pattern). The new PERS-007 rule fires on bad-consulting, validating the rule end-to-end against a fixture. Note: bad-saas-vendor matches `saas-customer` (not `saas-vendor`) because both playbooks share most features for a generic SaaS doc; sanity guard is playbook-agnostic. **Playbook fixture coverage: 8 → 10 of 12 launch playbooks.** Corpus: 10 → 12 fixtures. **436/436 passing + 2 intentional skips.**

### bad-sow + playbook coverage enforcement + Lighthouse CI (2026-05-12) — ✅ complete

Three substantive additions:
1. **`bad-sow.docx` (13th fixture)** — targets the `sow` playbook (child of `msa-general`). Matched `sow` at 0.9 confidence. Under-defined deliverables + scope-creep clause + 2%/month late fee + `[TBD]` placeholder + undefined `best efforts`. Fires STRUCT-013 + FIN-009 + OBLI-008.
2. **`tests/integration/playbook-coverage.test.ts`** — for every id in `LAUNCH_PLAYBOOK_IDS`, asserts that some committed fixture matches it under the deterministic matcher OR that it's listed in `EXEMPT_PLAYBOOK_IDS` with a stated reason. Today's exempt list: `generic-fallback` (implicit) and `saas-vendor` (overlap with saas-customer). **A new playbook added without a fixture now fails CI.** 13 assertions.
3. **Lighthouse CI workflow + budgets (LAUNCH.md row l)** — new `.github/workflows/lighthouse.yml` + `lighthouserc.json` run Lighthouse against the built `dist/` on every push and PR with the mobile-4G throttled preset. CI fails if FCP > 1500 ms, LCP > 2000 ms, TTI > 2000 ms, TBT > 200 ms, CLS > 0.1, or category scores drop below perf 0.85 / a11y 0.95 / best-practices 0.9 / SEO 0.9.

**Playbook fixture coverage: 10 → 11 of 12 launch playbooks. Only `generic-fallback` is uncovered, by design.** Test corpus: 12 → 13 fixtures. **453/453 passing + 2 intentional skips.**

## How to pick up where this left off

1. Read this file plus [`spec.md`](docs/spec.md) §26 step **N** where N is the first unchecked row.
2. Run the verification gate for the *previous* step to ensure nothing regressed (Step 0: `npm install && npm run typecheck && npm test && npm run lint && npm run build`; Step 1: open `site/index.html` in a browser, optionally `npm run dev`, run Lighthouse).
3. Implement the next step in a focused session, then update this table.

| 20 | Source-pinning protocol implementation | ✅ complete | Staleness detector at `dkb/build/v3/staleness.ts`: `normalizeForHash` (NFC + CRLF→LF + whitespace collapse + trim) + `sha256Hex` (Node `node:crypto`, never `eval`), `detectStaleness({nodes, fetchAuthority, hashFn?, nowIso?})` returns a `StalenessReport` with one row per drifted citation, `applyStalenessToRules` flips `enabled: false` on every rule whose `depends_on_dkb_nodes` overlaps the report, `unacknowledgedRows` filters by `(node_id, citation)` against the ack list, `statusFromReport` produces the UI footer payload `{dkb_last_validated_at, stale_citations_pending_review}`. CLI at `dkb/build/v3/check-staleness.ts` loads `dkb/fixtures/v3/nodes/*.json`, replays text from `dkb/fixtures/v3/snapshots/{sha256(url)}.txt` in offline mode, writes `staleness-report.json`, and exits non-zero when unacknowledged rows exist. Ack file at repo root `dkb-staleness-ack.yml` (empty `acknowledgments: []` by default; YAML parsed with `FAILSAFE_SCHEMA` per the security rules — never `yaml.load` unsafe). UI footer added to `site/index.html` (`<footer><p data-role="dkb-validation">…</p></footer>`); `src/ui/dkb-validation.ts` exposes `hydrateDkbValidation` (fetches `/dkb/v3/validation-status.json` cache-busted, validates the payload shape, renders into the footer spans, leaves the placeholder text on failure) and is wired from `src/ui/main.ts` on `DOMContentLoaded`. Tests (16/16 new, 549/549 total passing): `staleness.test.ts` (normalize + clean + drift + rule disable + ack filter + status), `check-staleness.test.ts` (full CLI round-trip with tmpdir nodes/ack — clean, drift, ack-respected, missing-ack-file, malformed-entry), `dkb-validation.ui.test.ts` (DOM render + happy-path fetch + bad payload + fetch failure under happy-dom). `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green. |

| 31 | Consistency-check engine and two-document mode | ✅ complete | Cross-document engine at `src/engine/consistency/` (`types.ts` + `runner.ts` + `_helpers.ts` + `rules/`): `runConsistency({rules, documents, dkb})` accepts ≥2 parsed v2 documents (`{doc_id, source_file_name, playbook_id, tree, extracted}`) and emits a `ConsistencyRun` with deterministic `result_hash` (SHA-256 over the run JSON with `result_hash`/`executed_at`/`elapsed_ms` blanked — same hash contract as the v2 runner). Findings are sorted by `(severity, rule_id, doc_id, start_offset)`. `kindOf(doc)` classifies playbook ids into `msa | baa | dpa | nda | sow | other`; rules declare `requires: DocKind[]` and the runner skips them (`ran=false`) when a required kind is missing. Seven initial rules under `src/engine/consistency/rules/rules.ts` per spec §27: **CC-001** BAA permitted uses no broader than MSA service scope (critical, 45 CFR § 164.504(e)); **CC-002** DPA processing purpose matches MSA services (warning, GDPR Art. 28(3)); **CC-003** DPA data categories not broader than MSA — flags health/biometric/genetic/financial/government-id/children's data appearing in the DPA's Annex I.B with no anchor in the MSA's services description (warning); **CC-004** BAA term aligns with MSA (warning) — passes when the BAA is explicitly co-terminous, fires when the BAA sets an independent term; **CC-005** governing-law alignment across any pair of documents (warning) — uses `extracted.jurisdictions` first, falls back to paragraph scan, canonicalizes the raw text before bucketing; **CC-006** notice-clause alignment (info); **CC-007** order-of-precedence consistency (warning) — fires when the MSA names itself controlling but operative `indemnification | aggregate liability cap | IP ownership | warranty` terms live only in the subordinate document. Every finding cites both contributing documents and quotes the conflicting paragraph from each (`excerpts: ConsistencyExcerpt[]`, length ≥ 2). Rules are pure: no IO, no time, no randomness; throws are swallowed by the runner with a zero-finding log entry. `findParagraph(doc, pattern)` matches against both paragraph text and the containing section heading so anchors like "Scope of Services" (typically headings) score. Runner-level wiring at `src/engine/runner.ts`: new `runEngineMulti({documents, dkb, consistencyRules?, executed_at?})` runs each document's single-doc engine in parallel via `Promise.all`, then the consistency pass. Engine barrel re-exports the consistency types, the runner, the registry, and `kindOf`/`findByKind`/`hasAllKinds` helpers. Tests at `src/engine/consistency/runner.test.ts` (20 passing): registry contract (seven CC-NNN rules, unique ids, `category: "consistency"`), `kindOf` classifier, determinism (identical `result_hash` on two runs), defensive errors (`< 2 documents` and duplicate `doc_id`), per-rule positive + negative cases for CC-001/002/003/004/005/006/007, the BAA-co-terminous escape (CC-004), the MSA-anchored sensitive category (CC-003), and finding ordering (severity rank monotone; CC-001 critical before CC-005 warning). `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **743/743 tests passing + 2 skips**. v2 `LAUNCH_RULES` determinism hash is untouched (the consistency engine is a parallel runner, not a v2 modification). Remaining work to call this step a launch-grade gate (deferred to Step 34's golden corpus): paired-fixture corpus from spec §15 (20 MSA+DPA / MSA+BAA / MSA+SOW pairs), per-pair baseline expected-consistency-findings JSONs, and the UI hookup for the multi-doc drop (Step 33). The current rules use conservative heuristics that prefer false negatives over false positives; calibration against real paired fixtures lands with Step 34. |

Returns `family: "unknown"` with `suggested_playbook: null` when no detector scores ≥ 1. `FAMILY_TO_PLAYBOOK` maps each family to the actual `src/playbooks/v3/<id>.json`. **`compliance-frame.ts`** — `defaultFramesForPlaybook(playbookId)` returns `{on, available, hint?}` over a 20-frame controlled vocabulary (`ComplianceFrame` union: HIPAA / GDPR / UK-GDPR / 8 US state laws / GLBA / FERPA / 4 international / NIST-AI-RMF / EU-AI-Act / FTC-ROSCA). Add a companion DPA or BAA."` shown next to the chip row. `toggleFrame(current, frame)` is an immutable list-toggle helper. **`multi-doc.ts`** — pure reducer for the multi-document drop zone (spec §62, `MAX_DOCUMENTS = 4`). `addDocument` returns `{ok, state}` or `{ok: false, state, reason}` with two failure modes (over-limit, duplicate id). `markAnalyzing` / `markComplete` / `markError` / `removeDocument` are immutable card transitions through the `queued → analyzing → complete|error` state machine. `setConsistencyEnabled` and `setConsistencyFindingsCount` carry the spec-§62 "run cross-document consistency (default on)" checkbox state. `isReadyForConsistency` is true when ≥ 2 cards are in a terminal state; `hasUsableConsistencyBundle` is true when ≥ 2 cards completed successfully. **`copy.ts`** — `EMPTY_STATE_COPY` carries the spec-§63 four-document headline and sub. `V3_ERROR_COPY` is a closed mapping over 7 error codes including the three spec-named error states ("this looks like a BAA but no Business Associate party is defined…", "this looks like SCC Module 2 but Annex I is empty…", "this looks like an ACORD 25 but the certificate-holder block is illegible…"); `v3ErrorMessage(code)` falls back to a generic message for unknown codes. | 38 | Threat-model update | ✅ complete | New "v3 additions" section appended to [`docs/threat-model.md`](docs/threat-model.md) covering five distinct attack surfaces and trust assumptions introduced by v3: **(1) DKB integrity** — the manifest carries `version` + `sources[]` + `dkb_node_version` + `dkb_node_last_validated_at`, the runtime loader validates the manifest shape with Zod, and every v3 citation carries `content_hash_at_pin = sha256(normalizeForHash(snapshotText))` so a tampered DKB JSON fails the hash check; **(2) the staleness gate** — when an upstream regulator URL drifts, the affected rule is `enabled: false` and the build exits non-zero unless the drift is explicitly acknowledged in `dkb-staleness-ack.yml`, leaving an auditable trail; **(3) the citation surface** — every v3 citation appears in three report places (inline `[N]`, §55 citation-index appendix with clickable URL, and the per-page footer's "Citations as of [DKB build date]" line), so a reader of a single printed page can verify the report against its source; **(4) the "consensus practice" AI disclaimer** — the AI-addendum playbook's ADDENDA-NNN rules carry the framing explicitly in their descriptions and the report's §59 disclaimer block reinforces it ("Failing one of these checks is not a regulatory violation. It is an observation worth a conversation with counsel."); **(5) the explicit non-promise** that v3 covers every regulator — unsupported regulators surface as `N/A` cells with a "not yet covered" note rather than silently passing. The section closes with a "what v3 still does not protect against" enumeration of four residual risks (regulator-URL 404 between weekly builds; consensus practice hardening into statute mid-period; adversarial drafting against deterministic regex patterns; jurisdictional carve-outs that v3 cannot reason about without a pattern). Each subsection follows the v2 threat-model rhythm: "what this protects against" + "what it does not protect against" / "how it might be bypassed." No new code; documentation only. `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **788/788 tests + 2 skips**. |

| 40 | v4 repo scaffolding + tagline change | ✅ complete | New v4 namespace skeleton committed: `src/extract/v4/` (placeholder `index.ts` exporting `classifyV4(extracted, body_text)` + the 16-bucket `V4SubDomain` union for the Step 42 classifier), `src/engine/rules/v4/<sub-domain>/` for all 16 sub-domains (commercial / governance / equity / m-and-a / real-estate / employment / settlement / ip-licensing / privacy-extended / healthcare / insurance / banking / construction / trust-estate / compliance-policy / regulatory-prose — each ships an `index.ts` exporting an empty `<RULESET>_RULES: readonly Rule[] = []` so the v4 aggregate compiles without a behavior change), `src/engine/rules/v4/index.ts` aggregate exporting `V4_RULES: readonly Rule[] = []`, `src/playbooks/v4/README.md`, `tests/v4/README.md` (mirrors the v3 test layout per Step 45–59), `dkb/build/v4/README.md` + `dkb/fixtures/v4/README.md` (Step 60 fetcher framework), top-level `V4.md` short index pointing to spec-v4.md, this build plan, the catalog, and cousin docs. **Tagline change** (spec §3): `site/index.html` `<h1 id="hero-h1">` flipped from "Drop a contract." to "Drop legal docs." — no test depends on the hero text.
