| 41 | Multi-document ingest (folder + zip + multi-file) | ✅ complete | New module at [`src/ingest/multi.ts`](src/ingest/multi.ts) (282 lines) and 19 unit tests at [`src/ingest/multi.test.ts`](src/ingest/multi.test.ts). **Caps** (spec §8): `MAX_FILE_BYTES = 50 MB` (unchanged from v1), `MAX_BUNDLE_BYTES = 200 MB` uncompressed, `MAX_BUNDLE_FILES = 50`. Cap violation emits the spec-mandated copy: `BUNDLE_CAP_MESSAGE = "Vaulytica analyzes up to 50 files / 200 MB at once. Split your bundle or upload fewer files."`. **Validation surface**: `classifyExtension(filename)` returns `"pdf" | "docx" | null` (case-insensitive); `rejectionForFilename(filename)` steers `.doc` to the v1 "save as .docx" message and everything else to the generic "accepts .pdf and .docx" message. **`planBundle(candidates)`** is the pure validator — returns `{ok: false, reason}` when bundle-level caps fail OR `{ok: true, entries, total_bytes}` with per-entry verdicts (one `MultiIngestEntry` per input, either `{ok: true, kind, bytes, size_bytes}` or `{ok: false, reason}`). **Browser-side enumeration**: `filesToCandidates(files: File[])` reads a `FileList` into the candidate-bundle shape; `enumerateFolderEntry(entry, out?)` recursively walks a `FileSystemEntry` (from `DataTransferItem.webkitGetAsEntry()` or the File System Access API), draining `readEntries` until empty (the W3C spec requires it because `readEntries` returns batches), and skips any non-`.pdf`/`.docx` leaf silently. **Zip extraction**: `extractZipEntries(archive: ArrayBuffer)` uses `fflate`'s synchronous `unzipSync` (pure JS, zero dependencies, MIT, no WebAssembly compile, no `eval` — works behind the strict CSP) and returns entries sorted lexicographically by basename so multi-document bundle hashes (spec §15) are stable regardless of zip-producer order. Directory entries are skipped, `__MACOSX/` sidecars are skipped silently, and zip-slip `..` traversal segments are defensively refused. Non-`.pdf`/`.docx` entries inside the zip are skipped silently (spec §8: user's intent is plainly the legal docs; a README.txt alongside a contract shouldn't fail the bundle). `looksLikeZip(bytes)` matches the PK magic (`\x50\x4b\x03\x04`, `\x05\x06` empty-zip, or `\x07` spanning) for the drop-zone routing decision. **`ingestEntries(entries, opts?)`** runs the existing single-file ingest paths (`ingestPdfBuffer` / `ingestDocxBuffer`) over an accepted bundle; per-file errors surface as rejections so a single corrupt file does not poison the whole bundle. **`ingestBundle(candidates, opts?)`** is the convenience wrapper that combines `planBundle` + `ingestEntries`. New dep: `fflate@^0.8.3` (28 KB unpacked, MIT, zero runtime deps, used both for §8 unzip and §11 bundle-zip output downstream). Ingest barrel re-exports the v4 surface alongside the v1 entries; v1 callers are untouched. Tests cover: `classifyExtension` case-insensitive matching + null on unknown; `rejectionForFilename` `.doc` and generic paths; `planBundle` cap enforcement (empty / > 50 files / > 200 MB / per-file > 50 MB / mixed valid + invalid extensions); `looksLikeZip` PK magic variants; `extractZipEntries` `.pdf`+`.docx` filtering, nested-folder basename flattening, `__MACOSX/` skip, deterministic ordering across two differently-ordered archives, defensive zip-slip behavior. All gates green: typecheck clean, lint clean, **810/810 tests + 2 skips**, build green. The browser `enumerateFolderEntry` path is not exercised by the unit tests because `FileSystemEntry` is a browser-only DOM API (the Playwright Step 41 follow-up will cover it under `tests/e2e/v4/`). The wiring into the UI dropzone (Step 33 carry-forward / spec §62 multi-doc drop UI) and the bundle pipeline (`runPipelineMulti` in `src/ui/pipeline.ts` consuming `ingestBundle` + `runEngineMulti`) are deferred to a focused follow-up commit so this commit stays scoped to ingest. |
| 42 | Document classifier (two-stage) | ✅ complete | Two-stage classifier shipped per spec §9. **Stage 1 (sub-domain)**: new module [`src/extract/v4/classifier.ts`](src/extract/v4/classifier.ts) (210 lines) implements `scoreSubDomains()` and `classifyV4SubDomain()` over all 16 §6 sub-domains using v2-aligned scoring weights (title 0.3, distinguishing 0.2, negative -0.1) and a per-domain ceiling that normalizes raw scores into `[0, 1]` regardless of feature-table size. **Stage 2 (family)** is delegated to the existing v2 `matchPlaybook` matcher run over playbooks under the winning sub-domain — that hookup lands when v4 ruleset playbooks land (Steps 45–59), so today `family_id: null` returns from the stage-1 winner. **v3 short-circuit**: when a `V3Detection` with confidence ≥ 0.6 is passed in, the classifier maps the v3 family directly to its v4 sub-domain + family via an explicit `v3FamilyToV4()` table (BAA→I.1, DPA-EU→I.2, DPA-US-state→I.3, SCC→I.4, UK-IDTA→I.5, COI→K.1, NDA-deep→A.3, MSA-deep→A.1, vendor-security→I.6, AI-addendum→O.8) so a confident v3 detection is not second-guessed. **Threshold (spec §9, open question 8)**: 0.5 for sub-domain (below which `sub_domain: null` falls through to v2 `matchPlaybook` and ultimately `generic-fallback`); 0.5 for family (below which the sub-domain's `*-generic` playbook runs, hookup deferred to the per-sub-domain steps). **Feature data**: [`dkb/v4/sub-domain-features.json`](dkb/v4/sub-domain-features.json) (≈ 350 lines) anchored to the §6 catalog — 16 sub-domains × {title keywords, distinguishing phrases, negative features}: A-commercial (18 keywords, 14 phrases), B-governance (15 / 15), C-equity (16 / 18), D-m-and-a (13 / 17), E-real-estate (16 / 16), F-employment (12 / 13), G-settlement (10 / 11), H-ip-licensing (10 / 11), I-privacy (20 / 15), J-healthcare (4 / 10), K-insurance (7 / 12), L-banking (12 / 14), M-construction (11 / 11), N-trust-estate (12 / 14), O-compliance-policy (16 / 13), P-regulatory-prose (10 / 11). Negative features are calibrated for the most common cross-domain confusions (e.g., E-real-estate's "premises / lessor / lessee / tenant" subtract from A-commercial, B-governance, F-employment). **Diagnostic surface**: `rankedAlternatives(input, n=3)` returns the top-N scoring sub-domains for the per-document report's "Detected as: X (confidence 0.83). Alternatives: Y (0.21)." line (spec §9). Tests at [`tests/v4/extract/classifier.test.ts`](tests/v4/extract/classifier.test.ts) (23 passing): one positive detection per non-A sub-domain (B / C / D / E / F / G / K / L / M / N / O / P) each above the 0.5 threshold; threshold fallback (no-signal body and low-signal body both return `sub_domain: null`); v3 short-circuit (high-confidence BAA→I.1, low-confidence falls through to v4 stage 1, unknown returns null); `rankedAlternatives` ordering; determinism (two runs of the same input produce `toEqual` classifications); registry contract (exactly 16 sub-domains; every entry has ≥ 1 title + ≥ 1 phrase; thresholds + weights match spec). The classifier is wired into `src/extract/v4/index.ts` as the `classifyV4(extracted, body_text, features, v3_detection?)` convenience entry; pipeline integration (calling `classifyV4` from `src/ui/pipeline.ts` and threading the result into the per-document report header) is deferred to the consolidated-bundle commit (Step 44) so the classifier ships standalone. `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **833/833 tests + 2 skips**. The v3 `matchPlaybook` flow remains the production path until Step 45+ playbooks register under the v4 sub-domains; the classifier is an additive surface today. |
| 43 | Consistency engine expansion | ✅ complete | Seven v4 CROSS-* rules ship under [`src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/`](src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/) on the existing v3 consistency engine, joining the seven v3 CC-NNN rules: **CROSS-PARTY-001** (info; detects party-name drift across documents — "Acme Corp." vs "Acme, Inc." canonicalize to the same entity after suffix-stripping but the originals diverge, surfaced because lenders / IP licensors / tax authorities care about the legal name on the executed copy); **CROSS-JURIS-001** (warning; complements v3 CC-005 which covers any-pair governing-law misalignment by firing only when 3+ documents are bundled together with 2+ different governing-law clauses — the precedence story at the bundle level requires an explicit recital); **CROSS-DEFTERM-001** (warning; flags defined terms with different definitions across documents — the looser definition controls in practice, the prevalent source of multi-doc litigation); **CROSS-DATE-001** (warning; detects effective-date chronology that is impossible — doc A dated 2026-01-01 references doc B which is itself dated 2026-06-01 by family name); **CROSS-AMOUNT-001** (warning; aggregate-liability-cap mismatch with the lower cap controlling for any conduct that touches both documents); **CROSS-MISSING-001** (warning; an operative document references a companion family by name — "DPA attached as Schedule B", "Business Associate Agreement" — but no document of that family is in the bundle); **CROSS-PRECEDENCE-001** (warning; complements v3 CC-007 which fires when MSA-controls + subordinate document has operative terms, by firing when two documents BOTH claim controlling status — "this Agreement shall control" in the MSA and "this SOW shall control" in the SOW). New helpers at [`src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/_helpers.ts`](src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/_helpers.ts): `normalizePartyName(name)` strips entity suffixes (Inc / Corp / LLC / L.P. / Ltd / Co / PLC / GmbH / SA / SARL / NV / AG / Pte / Sdn Bhd) + punctuation; `findPartyNameMismatches` dedupes parties per-document by canonical name + picks the longest original-name representative (the extractor sometimes returns the same party twice with subtly different boundaries — "Acme Corp.," vs "Acme Corp" — which would otherwise fire CROSS-PARTY against the same document); `findDefinedTermMismatches` walks `extracted.definitions.entries` to find terms with non-matching definitions; `effectiveDateOf` prefers the named-anchor "Effective Date" then falls back to the first absolute date; `firstLiabilityCap` scans for an aggregate-liability anchor and surfaces the highest dollar amount in the matched paragraph with scale-suffix parsing ("$1M" → 1,000,000). All rules use the existing v3 `ConsistencyRule` shape and `ConsistencyFinding` output — no new types added. Registry barrels: `src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/index.ts` exports `V4_CROSS_RULES` (length 7); `src/engine/consistency/rules/index.ts` adds `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES: readonly ConsistencyRule[] = [...V3_CC, ...V4_CROSS]` (length 14); the engine top-level barrel re-exports everything. Tests at [`src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/cross-doc-rules.test.ts`](src/engine/consistency/rules/v4/cross-doc-rules.test.ts) (**18 passing**): registry contract (7 rules, unique CROSS-CATEGORY-NNN ids), `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES` size invariant, one positive + one negative case per rule (Acme Corp / Acme Inc → CROSS-PARTY fires; identical-name → does not; 3-doc 2-law → CROSS-JURIS fires; 3-doc 1-law → does not; 2-doc → does not, CC-005 covers it; mismatched "Customer Data" definitions → CROSS-DEFTERM fires; matched → does not; MSA-Jan refs BAA-Jun → CROSS-DATE fires; MSA-Jul refs BAA-Jun → does not; $1M vs $50K caps → CROSS-AMOUNT fires; matched caps → does not; MSA refs DPA but no DPA in bundle → CROSS-MISSING fires; DPA present → does not; MSA-and-SOW-both-claim-control → CROSS-PRECEDENCE fires; only MSA claims → does not); determinism (V4_CROSS_RULES produces identical `result_hash` on two runs over the same bundle). **Test infrastructure fix**: discovered and fixed a race condition between `tests/integration/bundle-size.test.ts` and `tests/integration/sri.test.ts` — both shared `dist/`, the SRI test's `beforeAll` did `rmSync(DIST) + npm run build`, and the bundle-size test could land in the half-second window where `assets/` existed but `main-*.js` hadn't been written yet. Fix: bundle-size `beforeAll` now polls (up to 60s, `Atomics.wait` 250ms increments) for the eager `main-*.js` chunk to appear, falling back to running its own build only when `assets/` is genuinely empty. `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **851/851 tests + 2 skips**. The v3 CC-NNN engine is unchanged; `runConsistency` is a single deterministic engine that accepts either rule set or the combined `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES` registry. Wiring `ALL_CONSISTENCY_RULES` into `src/ui/pipeline.ts` and the consolidated bundle report (§59 → §11) is the Step 44 follow-up. |
| 44 | Consolidated bundle report renderer | ✅ complete | New module at [`src/report/bundle.ts`](src/report/bundle.ts) (~430 lines) ships the spec §11 consolidated bundle artifact set: **`buildBundleDocxReport(input)`** assembles the DOCX with cover (bundle fingerprint, document count, engine version, DKB version, cross-document-rules count, analysis date), executive summary (per-document totals + cross-document totals as a side-by-side table), per-document subsections (file name, detected family, playbook id, file SHA-256, per-document result hash, severity counts, and the top `BUNDLE_TOP_N = 10` findings per spec §11 — already in (severity, rule_id, document_position) order from the single-doc runner), cross-document consistency appendix (every `CROSS-*` finding with severity badge, description, explanation, recommendation, and one indented italic excerpt line per contributing document), deduped citation bibliography (built by walking per-doc findings first, then cross-doc findings — first-reference numbering, 1-based, deterministic), audit trail (engine + DKB + consistency-engine versions, per-doc playbook list with confidence, full per-doc and cross-doc rule execution logs with elapsed times), and the standard v1 §22 disclaimer block. **`buildBundleJson(input)`** returns `{ runs, cross_doc_findings, bundle_fingerprint, dkb_version, engine_version }` per spec §11; `buildBundleJsonBlob` wraps it in an `application/json` Blob (pretty-printed for humans). **`bundleFingerprint(per_doc_result_hashes)`** is `sha256(sorted-hashes joined by "\n")` — order-independent and deterministic; each per-doc `result_hash` already folds in `source_file.sha256`, so the bundle fingerprint covers both inputs and rule outcomes. **`buildBundleZip(input)`** produces an `application/zip` Blob containing `consolidated-report.docx` + `bundle.json` (and any `per_document_artifacts` entries placed under `per-document/`), entries written in lexicographic order with a fixed `mtime = 2000-01-01 UTC` per-entry so the zip envelope is byte-identical across runs (fflate refuses mtimes outside 1980–2099, which is why we cannot use `0`). The fflate dependency was already added in Step 41 for ingest; this commit consumes it for the §11 output path — one library, two paths, as the spec §11 footnote notes. Tests at [`src/report/bundle.test.ts`](src/report/bundle.test.ts) (**13 passing**): `bundleFingerprint` order-independence + 64-char hex + value sensitivity; `buildBundleJson` shape (runs.length, cross_doc_findings.length, fingerprint regex, versions); `buildBundleJsonBlob` MIME type + pretty-printed delimiter; bundle-JSON determinism via `JSON.stringify(a) === JSON.stringify(b)`; consolidated DOCX non-empty + OOXML MIME + ZIP `PK\x03\x04` magic; zero-cross-doc-findings rendering path; `BUNDLE_TOP_N === 10` invariant; bundle zip entry listing (`bundle.json` + `consolidated-report.docx`); bundle zip with `per_document_artifacts` placed under `per-document/`; bundle-JSON-inside-zip byte-identical across two runs (proof the JSON layer + zip framing are deterministic; the DOCX layer cannot be byte-identical because the `docx` library timestamps internally). `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **864/864 tests + 2 skips**. Pipeline integration (`src/ui/pipeline.ts` calling `runEngineMulti` + `buildBundleZip` and surfacing a download button) is the natural follow-up commit — `src/ui/pipeline.ts` is the only consumer that needs to know about the bundle artifact set. |

(b) byte-identical canonical output across two in-process runs (determinism); (c) the playbook match is a v4 playbook (not `generic-fallback`) and at least one finding is produced. Bundle goldens at [`tests/golden/v4/bundle-expected/`](tests/golden/v4/bundle-expected/) record per-doc `result_hash` + finding count and the consistency-run summary (`result_hash`, finding count, finding rule_ids, execution-log count) — they do not duplicate per-doc engine runs already covered under `expected/`. Regeneration pattern: `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1 npx vitest run tests/golden/v4`. `npm run typecheck && lint && test && build` all green; **1124/1124 + 2 skips** (was 1062 + 2; +62 new tests). Remaining: subsequent fixtures land per the recipe documented in [`tests/golden/v4/README.md`](tests/golden/v4/README.md). |

## Post-4.0 work

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (9 → 12) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced the v4 end-to-end fail-fixture corpus from nine to twelve fixtures, spanning three new v4 sub-domains (settlement, compliance-policy, construction), each deriving from the corresponding minimal-pass fixture by extending the preamble with a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include the load-bearing clause and dropping every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `settlement-confidential-missing-consideration-fail.txt` — Confidential Settlement Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned compensation clause stating the monetary amount to be paid for the releases set forth herein, relying instead on the delivery of non-monetary undertakings documented in a separately executed side letter. No "settlement payment / amount / sum", "consideration / in consideration", or "$NNN" dollar anchor appears anywhere in the document. **SET-006 (critical)** fires — its three present_patterns `/(settlement\s+payment|settlement\s+amount|settlement\s+sum)/i`, `/(consideration|in\s+consideration)/i`, and `/\$\s*[\d,]+/` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. Without recited consideration the agreement is vulnerable to a failure-of-consideration defense; the parties cannot verify the bargained-for exchange without a stated settlement payment amount.
- `compliance-anti-bribery-missing-third-party-diligence-fail.txt` — Anti-Bribery and Anti-Corruption Policy with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned counterparty-vetting section (deliberately avoiding "third party / parties", "agent(s)", "intermediary / intermediaries", "distributor", "due diligence", "screening", and "background"), relying instead on contractual representations and warranties obtained at onboarding. Neither third-party identification nor due-diligence review anchor appears anywhere in the document. **POL-007 (critical)** fires — its two present_patterns `/(third.?part(y|ies)|agents?|intermediar(y|ies)|distributor)/i` and `/(due\s+diligence|screening|background)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. DOJ-SEC FCPA Resource Guide identifies third-party intermediaries as the most common FCPA channel; without a vetting obligation the policy has no textual hook to trigger risk-based review before a high-risk engagement.
- `construction-contract-missing-contract-sum-fail.txt` — Construction Contract with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned pricing clause and a separately captioned payment-cadence clause (deliberately avoiding "contract sum", "stipulated sum", "guaranteed maximum price", "GMP", "cost-plus", "progress payments", and "payment schedule / terms"), relying instead on a separately negotiated fee letter and invoicing protocol. Neither the pricing model anchor nor the payment-cadence anchor appears anywhere in the document. **CON-003 (critical)** fires — its two present_patterns `/(contract\s+sum|stipulated\s+sum|guaranteed\s+maximum\s+price|gmp|cost.plus)/i` and `/(progress\s+payments?|payment\s+(schedule|terms))/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. AIA A101 §§ 4–5 require the contract sum and progress-payment schedule; without a stated pricing model and draw cadence the pricing basis for any change-order dispute is undefined.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected v4 playbook (`confidential-settlement` / `anti-bribery-policy` / `construction-contract`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins twelve fail-fixtures; goldens regenerated. LAUNCH row v4-b updated to "12 end-to-end fail-fixtures across 12 sub-domains". `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (test count captured in commit message).

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (6 → 9) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced the v4 end-to-end fail-fixture corpus from six to nine fixtures, spanning three new v4 sub-domains (m-and-a, ip-licensing, healthcare), each deriving from the corresponding minimal-pass fixture by extending the preamble with a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include the load-bearing clause and dropping every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `m-and-a-asset-purchase-missing-excluded-liabilities-fail.txt` — Asset Purchase Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned retained-obligations schedule enumerating the liabilities of Seller that Buyer is not assuming, relying instead on the general principle that Buyer assumes only those liabilities expressly set forth on the Assumed Liabilities schedule. No "excluded liabilities" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **MNA-023 (critical)** fires — its present_pattern `/excluded\s+liabilities/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. The structural advantage of an APA is that Buyer assumes only specifically-identified liabilities; without a broad Excluded Liabilities catch-all, Buyer faces unquantified successor-liability exposure for obligations it believed it had not assumed.
- `ip-licensing-copyright-missing-exclusivity-fail.txt` — Copyright License Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned grant-scope clause specifying whether the license is exclusive or non-exclusive (deliberately avoiding "exclusive", "non-exclusive", and "sole"). No "exclusive / non-exclusive / sole" anchor and no "in writing / signed / executed" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **IPL-020 (critical)** fires — its two present_patterns `/(exclusive|non.?exclusive|sole)/i` and `/(in\s+writing|signed|executed)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. Under 17 U.S.C. § 204(a) an exclusive copyright transfer must be in a signed writing; without a stated exclusivity designation neither party has a four-corners answer to whether the licensee holds exclusive or shared rights.
- `healthcare-phi-authorization-missing-expiration-fail.txt` — PHI Authorization with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned time-limit clause (deliberately avoiding "expir*", "on [digit]", "by [digit]", "years from", "end of", and "conclusion of"), relying instead on the patient's right to cancel the authorization by written notice as the operative mechanism for terminating the authorized use. No expiration date or event appears anywhere in the document. **HC-014 (critical)** fires — its two present_patterns `/(expir(es?|ation|ing)|expir\b)/i` and `/((on|by)\s+\d|years?\s+from|end\s+of|conclusion\s+of)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. 45 C.F.R. § 164.508(c)(1)(v) requires an expiration date or event; an authorization without one creates an open-ended consent that depends on patient revocation rather than natural lapse.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected v4 playbook (`asset-purchase-agreement` / `copyright-license` / `phi-authorization`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins nine fail-fixtures; goldens regenerated. LAUNCH row v4-b updated to "9 end-to-end fail-fixtures across 9 sub-domains". `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (test count captured in commit message).

### v4 fail-fixture corpus expansion (3 → 6) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced the v4 end-to-end fail-fixture corpus from three to six fixtures, spanning three new v4 sub-domains (equity, real-estate, banking), each deriving from the corresponding minimal-pass fixture by extending the preamble with a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include the load-bearing clause and dropping every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `equity-safe-missing-valuation-cap-fail.txt` — SAFE with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned economic-conversion-terms section setting out an investor-protection price ceiling, price reduction, or preferred-nation treatment, relying instead on the Company's next priced-round subscription documents as the operative mechanism for determining the conversion price. No "valuation cap", "discount rate", "most favored nation", or "MFN" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **EQT-003 (critical)** fires — its five present_patterns `/post.money\s+valuation\s+cap/i`, `/valuation\s+cap/i`, `/discount\s+rate/i`, `/most\s+favored\s+nation/i`, and `/\bmfn\b/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. Without at least one of cap, discount, or MFN the SAFE converts at the next-round price with no investor upside, defeating the economic purpose of the instrument.
- `real-estate-net-lease-missing-insurance-fail.txt` — Triple Net Lease with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned insurance-requirements section specifying tenant coverage types, minimum limits, additional-insured designations, and loss-payee arrangements, relying instead on a schedule of coverage certificates to be delivered before the Commencement Date. No "commercial general liability", "property insurance", or "waiver of subrogation" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **RE-003 (critical)** fires — its three present_patterns `/commercial\s+general\s+liability/i`, `/property\s+insurance/i`, and `/waiver\s+of\s+subrogation/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. NNN leases rely on tenant-carried insurance to protect both parties; without minimum CGL limits, additional-insured designation, and a waiver of subrogation, the landlord's coverage stack is exposed and recovery after a casualty is uncertain.
- `banking-loan-agreement-missing-events-of-default-fail.txt` — Loan Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned remedial-trigger schedule enumerating the circumstances under which the Lender may declare all outstanding principal and accrued interest immediately due and payable, relying instead on the Lender's rights under applicable law and the separate Credit Agreement. No "events of default", "cross-default", "cure period", "grace period", "insolvency", or "bankruptcy" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **BNK-012 (critical)** fires — its three present_patterns `/events?\s+of\s+default/i`, `/(cross.?default|cure\s+period|grace\s+period)/i`, and `/(insolvenc|bankruptc)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. Without an enumerated EoD catalogue with cure periods and a cross-default trigger, the lender cannot accelerate until maturity and loses the early-warning protection the EoD framework is designed to provide.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected v4 playbook (`safe-yc` / `net-lease` / `loan-agreement`). [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins six fail-fixtures; goldens regenerated. LAUNCH row v4-b updated to "6 end-to-end fail-fixtures across 6 sub-domains". `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (**1858 passing + 2 skips**).

### v4 fail-fixture corpus seed (0 → 3) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Seeded the v4 end-to-end fail-fixture corpus with three fixtures spanning three v4 sub-domains, modeled on the v3 fail-fixture pattern. Each fixture extends a minimal-pass document with a preamble sentence that affirmatively elects not to include the load-bearing clause, and drops every textual anchor that the rule's `present_patterns` look for. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v4/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v4/fixtures/):

- `governance-bylaws-missing-quorum-fail.txt` — Bylaws with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned meeting-threshold provision (deliberately avoiding the word "quorum"), relying instead on the residual default rule supplied by DGCL § 216 as the operative mechanism for determining the share-presence threshold at which a meeting of stockholders may transact business. No "quorum" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **GOV-005 (critical)** fires — its present_pattern `/quorum/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. DGCL § 216 supplies a majority-default if the bylaws are silent, but the bylaws themselves should restate the threshold explicitly; without a textual anchor, stockholders and proxy solicitors have no four-corners answer to what the meeting-threshold requirement is.
- `employment-executive-missing-severance-fail.txt` — Executive Employment Agreement with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned post-termination-pay schedule (deliberately avoiding the words "severance" / "salary continuation" / "COBRA"), relying instead on Employer's general termination-pay practices and the terms of any equity-plan documents as the operative mechanism for any post-employment compensation that may be payable. No "severance", "salary continuation", or "COBRA / continuation coverage" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **EMP-006** fires — its present_patterns `/severance/i`, `/salary\s+continuation/i`, and `/(cobra|continuation\s+coverage)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. Severance terms are the central economic feature of an executive agreement; a generic at-will-with-no-severance contract leaves the executive with no contractual hook for post-termination compensation.
- `privacy-cookie-notice-missing-categories-fail.txt` — Cookie Notice with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned categories-of-cookies section (deliberately avoiding "essential / functional / analytics / advertising / performance / targeting" anchors), relying instead on a published cookie inventory and the consent-management tool referenced in the notice. No "strictly necessary / essential", "functional / preferences", or "analytics / performance / targeting / advertising" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **PRV-001** fires — its three present_patterns `/(strictly\s+necessary|essential)/i`, `/(functional|preferences?)/i`, and `/(analytics|performance|targeting|advertising)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. ePrivacy Directive Art. 5(3) requires informed consent for non-strictly-necessary cookies; without a categorized inventory the user cannot give the granular consent the directive contemplates.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected v4 playbook (`bylaws-corporation` / `executive-employment` / `cookie-notice`). New test harness at [`tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v4/fixture-sanity.test.ts) — mirrors the v3 sanity-test pattern — pins three fail-fixtures and asserts the load-bearing rule fires on each. Goldens generated; LAUNCH row v4-b updated from "15 per-family fail fixtures (pre-existing unit-level)" to "3 end-to-end fail-fixtures across 3 sub-domains (golden + sanity)" with the unit-level coverage statement preserved. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (**1846 passing + 2 skips**).

### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (219 → 222) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from two-hundred-and-nineteen end-to-end fail-fixtures to two-hundred-and-twenty-two by adding three new fixtures, each targeting one of the last three v3 rules that lacked a dedicated end-to-end fail-fixture (ADDENDA-010, ADDENDA-018, DPA-051). With this batch every shipping v3 rule in `src/engine/rules/v3/` now has a dedicated end-to-end fail-fixture pinned in [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts). New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `ai-addendum-missing-ai-definitions-fail.txt` — AI Addendum with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned definitions section setting out the meanings of the core AI terms relied on throughout this AI Addendum, instead relying on the ordinary commercial usage of those terms as understood in the industry from time to time, and on the descriptions of Services contained in the MSA and the applicable Statement of Work, as the operative mechanism for resolving any ambiguity. Throughout the operative text the "generative AI" / "foundation model" / "large language model" / "LLM" / "training data" anchors are dropped (replaced with neutral phrasings such as "AI systems" and "model inputs"); the "(Output|Outputs) … (means|shall mean)" anchor is likewise absent. **ADDENDA-010 (warning)** fires — its three present_patterns `/(generative\s+AI|foundation\s+model|large\s+language\s+model|\bLLM\b)/i`, `/(\b)(Output|Outputs)\b.{0,40}(?:means|shall\s+mean)/i`, and `/training\s+data/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. NIST AI RMF and practitioner posture both expect definitions to anchor the operative obligations of an AI Addendum; without textual definitions, every other AI-addendum clause is exposed to ordinary-meaning drift (e.g., disagreement over whether a retrieval-augmented system is a "foundation model" within the scope of the prohibition).
- `eula-missing-eu-consumer-law-fail.txt` — EULA with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned EU-consumer-law-minimums clause referencing the European Union digital-content and consumer-rights directives by their formal citation, instead relying on a generic Section 10 consumer-protection-savings provision as the operative mechanism for any consumer-protection rights that may be asserted by an End User who happens to reside in the European Union. No "Digital Content Directive", "Directive (EU) 2019/770", "Consumer Rights Directive", or "Directive 2011/83" anchor appears anywhere in the document, and no "consumer rights cannot be limited / are not waived" phrasing appears either. **ADDENDA-018 (info)** fires — its present_patterns `/(Digital\s+Content\s+Directive|Directive\s+\(?EU\)?\s*2019\/770|Consumer\s+Rights\s+Directive|Directive\s+2011\/83)/i` and `/(consumer\s+rights\s+(?:cannot\s+be|are\s+not)\s+(?:limited|waived))/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. EU consumer law (Directive (EU) 2019/770 on digital content and digital services and Directive 2011/83/EU on consumer rights) cannot be contracted around for consumer-facing EULAs; a generic non-waiver savings clause does not put an EU consumer on textual notice of the directive-level minimums to which they are entitled (conformity, defects, remedies, withdrawal).
- `dpa-controller-processor-missing-notice-clause-fail.txt` — GDPR Controller-to-Processor DPA with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned formal-communications clause stating how formal communications between the parties (including breach notices and other written communications) are to be delivered, instead relying on the corresponding mechanism in the MSA as the operative mechanism. No "notice shall be" / "notice must be" / "notices under" / "notices hereunder" / "notices shall" / "notice address" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Section 10 (Breach Notification under GDPR Art. 33) is preserved but uses "inform" rather than the trigger phrase, and Section 14 (Survival) is preserved so DPA-052 still passes where it was passing. **DPA-051 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `/(notice\s+(shall|must)\s+be|notices\s+(under|hereunder|shall)|notice\s+address)/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. GDPR Art. 33(2) contemplates that the processor "shall notify" the controller of any personal data breach without undue delay; a DPA without a formal-communications clause leaves the parties without a textual anchor for the delivery method, addressee, and timing of breach notices and other communications that ride on top of that statutory duty.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected playbook (`ai-addendum` / `eula` / `dpa-controller-processor`). [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins two-hundred-and-twenty-two fail-fixtures (was two-hundred-and-nineteen); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule fires. Goldens regenerated; LAUNCH row v3-b updated to 222. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (**1834 passing + 2 skips**).

### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (216 → 219) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from two-hundred-and-sixteen end-to-end fail-fixtures to two-hundred-and-nineteen by adding three new fixtures, all targeting previously-uncovered rules within the AI Addendum playbook. None of the three load-bearing rules (ADDENDA-013, ADDENDA-015, ADDENDA-016) had a dedicated end-to-end fail-fixture before this batch. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `ai-addendum-missing-output-ownership-fail.txt` — AI Addendum with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned clause allocating, as between Customer and Vendor, the intellectual-property rights in the Outputs of any AI system, instead relying on the MSA's general intellectual-property provisions and Section 6 (Vendor Indemnity for AI-Generated IP Infringement) as the operative mechanism for handling any disputes arising in respect of such Outputs. No `(Output\w*).{0,40}(owns?|own|owned by|title to)` or reverse-direction anchor appears anywhere in the document. Section 2 (no-training-on-Customer-Data) is preserved so ADDENDA-011 still passes; Section 6 (IP indemnity) is preserved so the rest of the AI-addendum baseline still passes where it was passing. **ADDENDA-013 (warning)** fires — its present_patterns `/(Output\w*).{0,40}(?:owns?|own|owned\s+by|title\s+to)/i` and `/(?:owns?|own|owned\s+by).{0,40}Output\w*/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. NIST AI RMF and practitioner posture both expect an explicit ownership allocation of AI Outputs; relying on the MSA's general IP provisions alone does not resolve the foundation-specific ambiguity (vendors often claim derivative-work rights in Outputs by default).
- `ai-addendum-missing-subprocessor-disclosure-fail.txt` — AI Addendum with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned schedule identifying the third-party model providers Vendor relies on to deliver the AI features described in this AI Addendum, instead relying on the wholesale incorporation of the MSA's sub-contractor authorization mechanism and the MSA-level approved-vendor list as the operative mechanism for downstream model-provider approvals. No OpenAI / Anthropic / Google Gemini / Google Vertex / Cohere / Mistral / Hugging Face / Azure OpenAI / AWS Bedrock anchor and no "AI sub-processor", "model sub-processor", or "AI vendor" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **ADDENDA-015 (warning)** fires — its present_patterns `/(OpenAI|Anthropic|Google\s+(?:Gemini|Vertex)|Cohere|Mistral|Hugging\s*Face|Azure\s+OpenAI|AWS\s+Bedrock)/i` and `/(AI\s+sub[- ]?processors?|model\s+sub[- ]?processors?|AI\s+vendors?)/i` are no longer matched anywhere in the document. GDPR Art. 28(2) requires controller authorization (and disclosure) of every sub-processor in the chain; when an AI feature is powered by a third-party foundation model, the model provider itself is a sub-processor whose identity must be discoverable from the four corners of the AI Addendum.
- `ai-addendum-missing-fine-tuning-deletion-fail.txt` — AI Addendum with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned clause obligating Vendor to remove, on expiry of the MSA, any datasets derived from Customer Data that were used to adjust the parameters of a foundation model, instead relying on Section 2 (no-training-on-Customer-Data) and the MSA's general post-termination handling provisions as the operative mechanism for handling any such residual artifacts. No "delete fine-tuning data", "delete training data", "fine-tuning datasets … delete/destroy", or "model weights … delete/destroy" anchor appears anywhere in the document. **ADDENDA-016 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `/(delete\s+(?:fine[- ]tun\w+|training)\s+data|fine[- ]tun\w+\s+(?:data|datasets?)[^.]{0,80}(?:delet|destroy)|model\s+weights?[^.]{0,80}(?:delet|destroy))/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. GDPR Art. 17 (right to erasure) reaches Customer Data that has been assimilated into model parameters or fine-tuning datasets; relying on a prohibition against training plus a generic MSA wind-down clause does not give Customer a direct contractual hook to compel removal of any residual artifacts the prohibition was breached to create.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to `ai-addendum`. [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins two-hundred-and-nineteen fail-fixtures (was two-hundred-and-sixteen); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule fires. Goldens regenerated; LAUNCH row v3-b updated to 219. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green (**1825 passing + 2 skips**).

### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (213 → 216) (2026-05-21) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from two-hundred-and-thirteen end-to-end fail-fixtures to two-hundred-and-sixteen by adding three new fixtures, all targeting previously-uncovered rules within the Multi-State US DPA playbook (the last three uncovered USDPA-001..025 rules). None of the three load-bearing rules (USDPA-013, USDPA-014, USDPA-024) had a dedicated end-to-end fail-fixture before this batch. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `dpa-multi-state-us-missing-type-of-data-fail.txt` — Multi-State US DPA with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned schedule enumerating the kinds of consumer records the Service Provider handles, instead relying on the description of Services in the MSA and the Statement of Work as the operative mechanism for identifying the subject-matter of the processing. No "type of personal data/information" or "category/categories of personal data/information" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Every other clause (Business-Purpose, prohibited acts, VCDPA/CPA/CTDPA/UCPA processor obligations, sub-processor flow-down, consumer rights assistance, annual assessment, breach notification, deletion on termination, certification) is preserved so the rest of the USDPA-001..025 baseline still passes where it was passing. **USDPA-013 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `/(type|categor(?:y|ies))\s+of\s+(personal\s+)?(?:data|information)/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. Va. Code § 59.1-579 and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-1305 each require the processor contract to identify the type of personal data processed as a named element; without a textual anchor a regulator cannot determine the in-scope record set from the four corners of the DPA.

Each state's processor-contract statute (Va. Code § 59.1-579, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-1305, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-520, Utah Code § 13-61-301) requires the duration of the processing to be set out; relying on the MSA term alone leaves the controller without a DPA-level anchor to time-box the service provider's authority to handle the personal information.
- `dpa-multi-state-us-missing-data-minimization-fail.txt` — Multi-State US DPA with the preamble extended by a sentence that affirmatively elects not to include a separately captioned proportionality principle limiting the Service Provider's collection of personal information to what is required for the Business Purpose, instead relying on the Business-Purpose definition in Section 1 and the prohibited-acts enumeration in Section 2 as the operative mechanism for confining the Service Provider's collection to the disclosed scope. Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.100(c), Va. Code § 59.1-578, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-1304, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-520(a), and Utah Code § 13-61-201 each incorporate a data-minimization principle requiring collection limited to what is reasonably necessary and proportionate; without a DPA-level minimization anchor the controller has no textual hook to enforce the statutory floor against the service provider.

NIST SP 800-53 is the consensus practitioner baseline for vendor security addenda; a pure "industry-standard" commitment without an enumerated control list is unenforceable because it gives the customer no specific controls to verify, audit, or reference in a breach proceeding.
- `baa-missing-sanctions-policy-fail.txt` — BAA with the § 164.308(a)(1)(ii)(C) sanctions clause replaced by a "Personnel Conduct" section that affirmatively disclaims the controlled-vocabulary mechanism contemplated by 45 C.F.R. § 164.308(a)(1)(ii)(C): "The parties have elected not to adopt the controlled-vocabulary mechanism contemplated by 45 C.F.R. § 164.308(a)(1)(ii)(C) for a formal written personnel-accountability program requiring documented corrective action against staff who mishandle PHI, and instead rely on Business Associate's general employment-law and human-resources obligations as the operative personnel-accountability framework." No "(sanction|discipline) (policy|workforce|employees)" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Every other clause (Permitted Uses, Safeguards, Reporting, Subcontractor Flow-Down, Access/Amendment/Accounting, Books and Records, Return or Destruction, Minimum Necessary, Mitigation, Workforce Training, Encryption, Risk Assessment, Subcontractor List, Governing Law, Notice, Term, Signature) is preserved so the rest of the BAA-001..045 baseline still passes where it was passing. **BAA-034 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `/(sanction|discipline)\s+(policy|workforce|employees)/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. 45 C.F.R. § 164.308(a)(1)(ii)(C) requires covered entities and business associates to implement a sanctions policy for workforce members who fail to comply with the security policies and procedures of the entity; a BAA that affirmatively disclaims the controlled-vocabulary personnel-accountability framework leaves OCR without the § 164.308(a)(1)(ii)(C) hook it relies on when auditing business-associate workforce management.
- `msa-vendor-deep-missing-ai-usage-clause-fail.txt` — Vendor-form MSA with a new sentence in Section 2 (Services) that affirmatively disclaims any obligation to disclose whether Vendor uses automated reasoning, predictive, or machine-learning tooling in delivering the services, and explicitly states that "this Agreement does not incorporate by reference the NIST AI RMF transparency baseline or any other framework requiring disclosure of automated-tooling usage." No "artificial intelligence", "generative AI", "foundation model", "large language model", or "LLM" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Every other clause (Order of Precedence, Fees and Payment, Intellectual Property Ownership, Confidentiality, Limited Warranty, Mutual Indemnification, Limitation of Liability, Insurance, Termination, Governing Law, Entire Agreement) is preserved so the rest of the MSA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **MSA-028 (info)** fires — its present_pattern `/(artificial\s+intelligence|generative\s+AI|foundation\s+model|large\s+language\s+model|\bLLM\b)/i` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. NIST AI RMF establishes transparency about AI usage as the baseline consensus practice; an MSA that affirmatively disclaims disclosure of automated-tooling usage leaves Customer without the contractual hook to learn whether Vendor's outputs are AI-generated, whether Customer Data is used for model training, and who owns IP in AI-generated deliverables — all questions the AI Addendum playbook (§49) addresses only after the MSA-level AI-usage clause is confirmed present.

Many courts require a movant to post a bond as a condition of preliminary injunctive relief; a contractual waiver smooths the emergency-motion path, and a mutual NDA that names injunctive relief without waiving the bond leaves a delay-and-cost lever on the table that a determined leaker can exploit while disclosure is in flight.
- `dpa-ccpa-service-provider-missing-purpose-limitation-fail.txt` — CCPA Service-Provider Addendum that names the Service Provider designation and recites the "same level of privacy protection" standard from Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.140(ag) but never anchors the use of Personal Information to the "specific business purpose enumerated" framing required by § 1798.140(ag)(1)(B). Section 2 ("Permitted Processing") rewrites the canonical anchor as "solely as reasonably necessary and proportionate to perform the Services described in the MSA" and Section 3(c) generalizes the use-limitation to "any commercial purpose other than performing the Services described in the MSA". No "specific business purpose", "enumerated", or "business purpose enumerated" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the USDPA-001..025 baseline still passes where it was passing. **USDPA-001 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `(?:specific\s+business\s+purpose|enumerated\s+(?:in\s+this\s+)?(?:contract|agreement)|business\s+purpose\s+enumerated)` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.140(ag)(1)(B) requires the contract to prohibit the service provider from retaining, using, or disclosing Personal Information for any purpose other than the specific business purpose enumerated; "reasonably necessary and proportionate" language without the statutory anchor leaves the business exposed to enforcement under § 1798.155 if the service provider's processing drifts beyond the enumerated purpose set.
- `vendor-security-addendum-missing-audit-or-soc2-fail.txt` — Vendor Security Addendum with Section 1 rewritten from certifications subsections (SOC 2 Type II + ISO 27001) to a generic "written information-security program aligned with prevailing industry practice" paragraph that delivers only an executive summary on request; Section 6 ("Verification") is rewritten to explicitly disclaim any customer-initiated audit privilege and to forbid reliance on any third-party assurance framework or certification scheme. The encryption, MFA, and vulnerability-management sections are preserved (so ADDENDA-001 and ADDENDA-005 still pass), but no "right to audit", "Customer ... audit", "SOC 2", "ISO 27001", "ISO/IEC 27001", or "in lieu of (an) audit" anchor appears anywhere in the document. Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the ADDENDA-001..009 baseline still passes where it was passing. **ADDENDA-003 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `(right\s+to\s+audit|customer.{0,40}audit|SOC\s*2|ISO\s*27001|ISO\s*\/IEC\s*27001|in\s+lieu\s+of\s+(?:an\s+)?audit)` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. Customers must be able to verify the vendor's security posture either directly (audit) or via an independent attestation (SOC 2 / ISO 27001); a "self-assessment plus executive summary" posture leaves the customer with no enforceable verification mechanism.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to its expected playbook (`mutual-nda-deep` / `dpa-ccpa-service-provider` / `vendor-security-addendum`). [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins one-hundred-and-sixty-five fail-fixtures (was one-hundred-and-sixty-two); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule fires. Goldens regenerated; LAUNCH row v3-b updated to 165. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green; **1663/1663 tests + 2 skips**.

GDPR Art. 28(3)(g) requires the processor, at the choice of the controller, to delete or return all personal data to the controller after the end of the provision of services — an "inventory and basis for retention" substitute leaves the personal data on the processor's systems and inverts the statutory default.

### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (141 → 144) (2026-05-19) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from one-hundred-and-forty-one end-to-end fail-fixtures to one-hundred-and-forty-four by adding three new fixtures spanning three distinct DPA-GDPR failure modes (hand-waving security language, missing personal-data scope annex, missing signature block) — none of the three load-bearing rules (DPA-023, DPA-038, DPA-043) had an end-to-end fail-fixture before this batch. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `dpa-controller-processor-hand-waving-security-language-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 6 (Security Measures (Article 32 GDPR)) augmented with an injected closing sentence: "To the extent any of the foregoing cannot be operationally implemented, Processor shall instead apply commercially reasonable security measures consistent with prevailing market practice for service providers of similar size and scope." Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-023 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `commercially\s+reasonable\s+(security|measures)` end-to-end. GDPR Art. 32 requires measures appropriate to the risk; "commercially reasonable" or "industry-standard" language without a specific Annex of technical and organisational measures is the hand-waving the regulator has criticised, because it shifts the substantive duty from a defined set of controls to whatever the processor's market peers happen to be doing.
- `dpa-controller-processor-missing-personal-data-annex-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 2 (Categories of Personal Data and Data Subjects) rewritten to reference "the Categories of Personal Data Section" at the end of the DPA instead of "Annex I"; the Annex I heading at the end of the DPA is likewise renamed to "Categories of Personal Data" with no "Annex I" / "Appendix I" / "Schedule I" / "Exhibit I" prefix. Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-038 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `(annex|appendix|exhibit|schedule)\s+(I|1|A)` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. SCC Annex I (and the modern DPA convention of an Annex describing the parties, transfer scope, and processing operations) anchors the description of the personal-data scope; without a labelled annex/appendix the document loses the canonical attachment that supervisory authorities and downstream subprocessors look to when scoping the processing.
- `dpa-controller-processor-missing-signature-block-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with the entire signature block (party headers + "Signed by:" lines + "Title:" lines including "Authorized Representative" + "Date:" lines) replaced with a single recital paragraph: "This DPA is executed on behalf of Globex Inc. (Controller) and Wayne Enterprises LLC (Processor) through their respective representatives, with execution evidenced solely by reference to the MSA cover page; no separate execution lines, witness lines, or attestation blocks are included in this DPA." Every other clause (including "Effective Date: February 1, 2026.") is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-043 (warning)** fires — its present_pattern `By:\s*[_\-\s]+|signature\s+block|authori[sz]ed\s+(signatory|representative)|sign(ed)?\s+by` is no longer matched anywhere in the document. GDPR Art. 28(9) requires the DPA to be in writing including in electronic form; a signature block — even on an electronic agreement — is the canonical evidence-of-execution artefact that supervisory authorities and counter-parties look to when establishing that the obligations attached to a named, authorised representative of each party.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to the `dpa-controller-processor` playbook so the auto-detect cannot drift to a v2 fallback. ### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (138 → 141) (2026-05-19) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from one-hundred-and-thirty-eight end-to-end fail-fixtures to one-hundred-and-forty-one by adding three new fixtures covering three GDPR-DPA vendor-overreach language-rule failure modes (unilateral deviation from instructions, controller indemnifies processor for GDPR fines, audit cost allocated entirely to controller) — none of the three load-bearing rules (DPA-037, DPA-048, DPA-049) had an end-to-end fail-fixture before this batch. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `dpa-controller-processor-instructions-deviation-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 4 (Documented Instructions Only) augmented with an injected sentence: "Notwithstanding the foregoing, Processor may deviate from Controller's instructions where, in Processor's reasonable judgment, such deviation is necessary or appropriate to operate the Services, and Processor shall not be required to seek prior approval from Controller before doing so." Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-037 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `processor\s+may\s+(deviate|depart)\s+from` end-to-end. GDPR Art. 28(3)(a) requires processing only on documented instructions from the controller; any deviation must be required by law and the processor must inform the controller — a unilateral "Processor may deviate" license collapses the statutory accountability chain and removes the controller's ability to direct the processing.
- `dpa-controller-processor-controller-indemnifies-gdpr-fines-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with a new Section 14 ("Indemnification") appended: "Controller shall indemnify, defend, and hold harmless Processor and its officers, directors, and employees from and against any GDPR fines, penalties, administrative sanctions, supervisory-authority claims, and related defense costs arising out of or relating to the processing of personal data under this DPA, regardless of the underlying cause or the party at fault." Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-048 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `controller\s+(shall|will)\s+indemnif.*?(processor|GDPR|fine)` end-to-end (both "Processor" and "GDPR" / "fine" anchors are within the matched span). Under GDPR Art. 82, a processor remains liable for its own infringements; shifting that liability to the controller through an unconditional indemnity is vendor overreach and may be unenforceable to the extent it purports to absolve the processor of supervisory-authority sanctions attributable to its own conduct.
- `dpa-controller-processor-audit-cost-controller-exclusive-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 11 (Audit and Inspection Rights) augmented with an injected closing sentence: "Controller shall bear all costs of any audit conducted under this Section, including any audit that uncovers a material breach by Processor." Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-049 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `controller\s+(shall|will)\s+bear\s+(all|the\s+entire|the\s+full)\s+costs?\s+of\s+(any\s+)?audit` end-to-end. Standard practice under GDPR Art. 28(3)(h) splits routine-audit cost to the controller but allocates cost to the processor where the audit uncovers material breach; a clause that fixes the entire audit cost on the controller — including breach-confirmed audits — discourages the controller from ever exercising the audit right and effectively immunizes processor non-compliance.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to the `dpa-controller-processor` playbook so the auto-detect cannot drift to a v2 fallback. Goldens regenerated; LAUNCH row v3-b updated to 141. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green; **1591/1591 tests + 2 skips**.

### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (135 → 138) (2026-05-19) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from one-hundred-and-thirty-five end-to-end fail-fixtures to one-hundred-and-thirty-eight by adding three new fixtures spanning three more GDPR-DPA failure modes (breach-notice content elements, breach-notice timing too loose, SOC 2 substitution eliminating audit) — none of the three load-bearing rules (DPA-026, DPA-027, DPA-036) had an end-to-end fail-fixture before this batch. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `dpa-controller-processor-missing-breach-content-elements-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 2's heading rewritten from "Categories of Personal Data and Data Subjects" to "Categories of Personal Data and Types of Data Subjects" and the body's "The categories of data subjects are..." line rewritten to "The types of data subjects are..."; the rest of the DPA is preserved so the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing, and no remaining text uses `nature\s+of\s+the\s+(personal\s+data\s+)?breach`, `categor(?:y|ies)\s+of\s+data\s+subjects`, `likely\s+consequences`, or `measures\s+taken`. **DPA-026 (warning)** fires — GDPR Art. 33(3) requires the breach notification to describe the nature of the breach, the categories and approximate number of data subjects affected, the DPO contact, the likely consequences, and the measures taken; a DPA whose Section 10 recites only that Processor will provide "sufficient information" without anchoring the Art. 33(3) content list leaves the controller without a contractual hook to demand the statutorily required elements when the BA hands over its intake report.
- `dpa-controller-processor-breach-notice-30-day-window-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 10 (Breach Notification) rewritten to a single sentence: "Processor shall notify Controller of any personal data breach no later than 30 days after becoming aware of the breach...". The 48-hour anchor is dropped in favor of a 30-day window; every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-027 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `\b(within|no\s+later\s+than)\s+(?:1[0-9]|2[0-9]|3[0-9]|[4-9][0-9]|[1-9][0-9]{2,})\s+days?\b.{0,80}(breach|notif)` end-to-end ("no later than 30 days after becoming aware of the breach"). Although GDPR Art. 33(2) does not set a strict outer bound for processor notification, supervisory guidance treats anything beyond ~24–72 hours as suspect; a 30-day processor-notification window leaves the controller no margin to meet its own Art. 33 / 34 obligations and effectively shifts the supervisory-notification clock entirely onto the controller.
- `dpa-controller-processor-soc2-eliminates-audit-fail.txt` — Controller→processor GDPR DPA with Section 11 (Audit and Inspection Rights) rewritten to keep the first information-production sentence but replace the "allow for and contribute to audits, including inspections" clause with "Processor's annual SOC 2 Type II report shall satisfy Controller's audit rights under this DPA in lieu of any on-site inspection, and the SOC 2 Type II report shall be the sole means of verifying Processor's compliance with this Section." Every other clause is preserved so the rest of the DPA-001..030 baseline still passes where it was passing. **DPA-036 (warning)** fires — its first bad_pattern matches `(SOC\s*2|ISO\s*27001).{0,160}(in\s+lieu\s+of|shall\s+(satisfy|fulfill|fulfil)|the\s+sole\s+means)` (both `shall satisfy` and `in lieu of` / `sole means` anchors are present) end-to-end. GDPR Art. 28(3)(h) requires the processor to allow for and contribute to audits; SOC 2 / ISO substitution is permitted as a default, but it must not eliminate the controller's right to an on-site audit on reasonable cause, and a contract that designates SOC 2 as the "sole means" of verification breaches the statutory floor.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to the `dpa-controller-processor` playbook so the auto-detect cannot drift to a v2 fallback. An effective date anchors the timing rules in the DPA (subject-matter window, breach-notice clock, deletion-or-return 30-day timer); without it, the Art. 28(3) intro requirement that the DPA define the duration of processing is undischarged on the face of the document.

Without the recital the BA has no contractual hook to limit downstream PHI requests, breaking the use/disclosure narrowing the Privacy Rule contemplates.
- `dpa-ccpa-service-provider-missing-no-combining-restriction-fail.txt` — CCPA Service-Provider Addendum with §3(d) (the no-combining-with-other-data restriction) removed and the §3 enumeration ending at (c); every other anchor for the combining prohibition — `combin\w+\s+(personal\s+information|the\s+personal\s+data)`, `7050\(c\)`, or `other\s+sources` — is absent from the rest of the document so no other paragraph supplies the missing recital. Sections 4 (Certification), 5 (Consumer Rights Assistance), 6 (Subprocessors), 7 (Security), 8 (Deletion or Return), and 9 (Audit) are preserved so the rest of the USDPA-001..025 baseline still passes where it was passing. **USDPA-004 (warning)** fires — Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.140(ag)(1)(D) requires the service-provider contract to prohibit combining the business's Personal Information with data the service provider receives from or collects in connection with any other person, business, or direct consumer interaction (except as 11 C.C.R. § 7050(c) narrowly permits); a contract silent on combining leaves the business exposed to enforcement risk under § 1798.155 if the service provider augments the data with off-platform signals.
- `scc-module-2-missing-onward-transfer-terms-fail.txt` — SCC Module 2 with §8.6 (Onward Transfers) removed entirely and the subsequent §8.7 ("Processing Under Authority of Data Exporter") renumbered to §8.6; every anchor for the onward-transfer recital — `onward\s+transfer`, `clause\s+8\.7`, or `clause\s+8\.8` — is absent from the rest of the document so no other paragraph supplies the missing reference. Clauses 8.1 through 8.5, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14, 15, 16, the docking clause, and the three annexes are preserved so the rest of the TRANSFER-001..019 baseline still passes where it was passing. **TRANSFER-020 (warning)** fires — EU SCCs Clause 8.7 / 8.8 governs onward transfers of personal data to third parties outside the EEA; an SCC Module 2 transfer arrangement that is silent on onward-transfer terms leaves the data exporter without a contractual mechanism to ensure that downstream recipients are bound by equivalent safeguards, defeating the Article 46 Schrems II protection chain.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to the relevant v3 playbook so the auto-detect cannot drift to a v2 fallback. [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins one-hundred-and-twenty-three fail-fixtures (was one-hundred-and-twenty); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule fires. Goldens regenerated; LAUNCH row v3-b updated to 123. `npm run lint && typecheck && test && build` all green.

- `mutual-nda-deep-missing-purpose-narrow-framing-fail.txt` — Mutual NDA with §3 (Use Restriction) and §4 (Obligations of Receiving Party) rewritten so the "solely for the Permitted Purpose" framing is replaced with open-ended "in connection with the Engagement" language, and the recital "Permitted Purpose" definition is dropped in favor of a vague "matter described in the parties' written correspondence." The Texas anchor and the indemnity-for-indemnitee-negligence sit in the same sentence so the intra-sentence `[^.]{0,400}` window in MSA-029's bad_pattern captures the pairing. Section 7 mutual indemnification, Section 8 cap-with-carveouts, and the other MSA-deep clauses are preserved so the rest of the baseline still passes. **MSA-029 (warning)** fires — Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ch. 151 § 151.102 voids construction-contract indemnities that cover the indemnitee's own negligence (with narrow insurance-policy exceptions); the rule surfaces the void-on-its-face exposure that the Texas-law clause inherits. MSA-010 (NY anti-indemnity) also fires because its construction-indemnity pattern is jurisdiction-neutral, but MSA-029 is the load-bearing detector for the Texas failure mode.

The rule does not assert wrongness; it surfaces the carve-out so the discloser can make a deliberate choice about whether to keep it, because a residuals clause materially weakens NDA protection for the disclosing party by allowing the receiver's personnel to keep using general knowledge after the relationship ends.

A broad feedback grant can sweep in customer ideas the customer may want to commercialize separately; the practitioner fix is to limit the feedback license to the vendor's product improvement and add a scope cap.

- `msa-vendor-deep-governing-law-venue-mismatch-fail.txt` — Vendor MSA with Section 11 collapsed to a single sentence that names Delaware as the governing law and New York County courts as the forum — the governing-law / venue alignment is broken and a Delaware-courts→Delaware-law symmetric structure is replaced by a Delaware-law→New-York-courts mismatch. **MSA-024 (info)** fires — its bad_patterns catch a `governed by the laws of {State A}` clause followed within 400 non-period characters by a `(courts|venue|jurisdiction|forum)` reference to a different `{State B}`; choosing one state's law but another state's forum forces the forum court to apply foreign law, adding cost and uncertainty.

Gen. Oblig. § 5-322.1 voids construction-contract indemnities that require the indemnitor to indemnify the indemnitee for the indemnitee's own negligence; the rule's first bad_pattern catches `indemnif\w+ … for any and all claims … including … negligence of the indemnitee` end-to-end and surfaces the void-on-its-face exposure the New-York-law clause inherits.

The Clause 14 heading retains "Clause 14" so TRANSFER-007 (presence of Clause 14) still passes; Clause 15 public-authority and Clause 16 non-compliance survive so TRANSFER-008 / 009 still pass. **TRANSFER-019 (critical)** fires — EDPB Recommendations 01/2020 require the parties to anchor a Transfer Impact Assessment (TIA) — the assessment of local laws and practices of the recipient country plus any supplementary measures — in the SCC; a bare "documented internal review" without the named statutory anchors does not satisfy the Schrems II / EDPB expectation.

The remaining Section 10 keeps the "personal data breach … notify Controller … within 48 hours" anchor so DPA-024 (Art. 33(2) presence) still passes; Section 2 retains "categories of data subjects" so DPA-026 still passes; the 48-hour window is in hours, not days, so the DPA-027 loose-timing `bad_pattern` (`within\s+\d+\s+days?`) does not fire. **DPA-025 (warning)** fires — GDPR Art. 33(2) uses the "without undue delay" standard and drafters should preserve the exact phrasing so the processor's reporting trigger maps cleanly onto the controller's Art. 33(1) 72-hour clock; "promptly" is a softer standard that does not carry the same supervisory-authority expectation.

Every downstream BAA clause (Reporting, Safeguards, Subcontractor Flow-Down, Access/Amendment/Accounting, Books and Records, Return or Destruction, Breach Notification) is preserved so BAA-001..022 still pass. **BAA-023 (warning)** fires — its `bad_patterns` catch both `Security\s+Incident.{0,200}successful\s+(unauthorized|access)` and `only\s+successful\s+(unauthorized\s+access|incidents)`; OCR's interpretation of 45 C.F.R. § 164.304 is that "Security Incident" includes both successful and unsuccessful attempts, so narrowing the definition to "only successful" lets material attack telemetry (failed login storms, port scans, unsuccessful intrusion attempts) escape the BA's Security Rule risk-management and reporting duties.
- `dpa-multi-state-us-missing-cross-context-prohibition-fail.txt` — Multi-state US DPA with Section 2(b) rewritten from "share personal information for cross-context behavioral advertising as defined in Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.140(ah)" to "make personal information available to any third party for targeted advertising purposes outside the Business Purpose"; every `cross[- ]context\s+behavioral\s+advertising` anchor is removed from the entire DPA. Section 2(a) sell-prohibition, Section 2(c) Business-Purpose limitation, and Section 2(d) no-combining restriction are preserved so USDPA-002 / 005 / 007 / 008 still pass. **USDPA-003 (critical)** fires — Cal. Civ. Code § 1798.140(ag)(1)(A) requires the service-provider contract to prohibit sharing including for cross-context behavioral advertising as a named statutory category; a generic "targeted advertising" prohibition is not equivalent because CCPA / CPRA enforcement turns on the specific "cross-context behavioral advertising" statutory term of art.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar pinning it to the relevant v3 playbook so the auto-detect cannot drift to a v2 fallback. - `dpa-controller-processor-missing-subprocessor-authorisation-fail.txt` — Controller-to-Processor DPA with Section 7 ("Subprocessors") rewritten to omit any "prior written authorisation" / "authorisation of Controller" anchor — the surviving clause permits Processor to engage subprocessors at will, preserving only a downstream notice + objection right and the flow-down obligation. **DPA-015** fires — GDPR Art. 28(2) requires the processor not to engage another processor without prior specific or general written authorisation; with the anchor stripped the contractual hook for Art. 28(2) is lost and the controller has no upstream veto over subprocessor onboarding.
- `vendor-security-addendum-missing-pen-test-cadence-fail.txt` — Vendor Security Addendum with Section 3 rewritten so that "Annual Penetration Test" becomes "Independent Penetration Test" and the cadence is described as "on a periodic basis as determined by Vendor's risk-management function"; every `annual\w*` / `annually` / `quarter\w+` / `every \d+ months/years` anchor adjacent to "penetration test" / "pen-test" is stripped. **ADDENDA-009 (info)** fires — annual third-party pen-tests are the practitioner-accepted baseline for SaaS; without a stated cadence the addendum carries no operational commitment to testing frequency.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar. ### v3 fail-fixture corpus expansion (39 → 42) (2026-05-18) — ✅ complete

Advanced LAUNCH row v3-b coverage from thirty-nine end-to-end fail-fixtures to forty-two by adding a new NDA third-party-exclusion fixture, a new vendor-MSA force-majeure fixture, and a new BAA cure-infeasible-termination fixture — each exercises a distinct load-bearing rule not previously covered. New fixtures under [`tests/golden/v3/fixtures/`](tests/golden/v3/fixtures/):

- `mutual-nda-deep-missing-third-party-exclusion-fail.txt` — removes the "third party lawfully obtained" prong from Section 2 (Carveouts); the last sentence actively reincorporates any information accessible from "any external party not operating under a separate written NDA". **NDA-D-008 (warning)** fires because its present_patterns require "third party" within ~80 chars of "without (breach|restriction)|lawfully" or "received/obtained from a third party" and now no such pairing appears; without this exclusion the Receiving Party risks breaching the NDA for using identical information it legitimately obtained from an independent source.
- `msa-vendor-deep-missing-force-majeure-fail.txt` — rewrites the force-majeure clause as a vendor-only "Excused Performance" paragraph (Vendor's obligations excused; Customer's payment obligations explicitly not excused) with no bilateral "neither party" or "either party" framing anywhere. **MSA-022 (info)** fires because its present_patterns require "(neither party|either party).{0,80}force majeure" or "force majeure.{0,160}(neither|both|each party)" and now neither pattern appears; a one-sided force-majeure clause is commercially abnormal and leaves the customer without contractual relief for its own performance obligations during a force-majeure event.
- `baa-missing-cure-infeasible-termination-fail.txt` — rewrites the Term and Termination section to allow only cure-period and insolvency termination, with no "cure is not feasible", "cure is infeasible", "infeasible to cure", or "fail.*cure" language anywhere in the document. **BAA-012 (warning)** fires because 45 C.F.R. § 164.504(e)(2)(iii) and HHS guidance expect BAAs to permit termination when cure of a material breach is not feasible; without this provision the covered entity may be left with no clear contractual exit when a systemic HIPAA violation cannot be remediated within the cure window.

Each fail-fixture has a `.playbook` sidecar forcing the v3 playbook. [`tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts`](tests/golden/v3/fixture-sanity.test.ts) now pins forty-two fail-fixtures (was thirty-nine); each entry asserts the load-bearing rule is in the fired set. Goldens regenerated via `VAULYTICA_REGEN_GOLDEN=1`.
